Current Affairs Commentary

Appealing on Behalf of Disaster Victims 23

— Du

In recent days, the water level of the Yangtze River has been receding. The people in the Wuhan area are fortunate to have avoided the disaster of becoming fish food. The Yellow River's torrents have not yet reached Weishan Lake, and northern Jiangsu also seems to be without immediate danger. Although the autumn flood season has not yet passed and the future is still uncertain, the current situation can be tolerated for the time being. In this time of initial respite, the issue that concerns us the most is the resettlement of the people in the disaster areas. According to the statistics of the Hubei Provincial Disaster Relief Association, in the disaster-stricken areas of 49 counties, there are 7,149,712 disaster victims. In other provinces such as Hebei, Shandong, Henan, Anhui, Hunan, and Jiangxi, the number of disaster victims gathered and awaiting relief may be even higher than this number. The funds required for relief, just for Hubei Province alone, already require 19 million yuan. Combined with the expenses of the whole country, the amount will be even more alarming. Recalling the government's depleted treasury, there is a risk of being unable to make ends meet at any time. Even if preparations are sufficient, the huge amount needed to cope with the flood control effort is already a cause for concern. The plan for post-disaster recovery seems even more difficult to implement.

Nevertheless, human beings are most endowed with the sympathy of weighing and considering [others' needs]. Natural disasters occur in every country from time to time. Even enemies think about showing sympathy. The event of Qin and Jin sailing boats together is a beautiful story passed down through the ages. Moreover, we all live in the same region, sharing weal and woe. Fortunately, we have not been affected by the flooding, and we are able to protect ourselves with our families and children after having our fill. Thinking of the disaster victims in the flooded areas of the north and south, who are exposed to the wind and dew and crying for food, their situation of being displaced, wandering, and helpless can be imagined without the need for elaborate description. Since we are all human beings, how can we not have feelings of fear and compassion? We should reduce our clothing and food consumption and contribute generously. Even if a drop in the bucket is not enough, it can be gathered to form a fur coat. When things have come to this point, we should not consider the effectiveness, but only do our best to respond to the situation to put our minds at ease. As for the government's relief funds, if they can raise a substantial amount, they should determine the steps to take and manage them in a unified manner. Emergency relief is indeed a timely measure, but there should be a permanent plan for post-disaster recovery. For example, if there are 7 million disaster victims, the number of educated men and women, children of school age, and those with construction skills among these 7 million people should be clearly investigated and provided with places to settle down separately. The remaining personnel who cannot be settled may as well be used as the backbone team for water management. With the relief funds as capital and the disaster victims as labor, we can start the dredging project. When the pain is just beginning to be felt, and the past is not forgotten, it is easier to achieve results by considering the time and effort. Moreover, if this is used to appeal to the public, the relief funds will have a twofold meaning, and the willingness to donate will surely be greatly increased. It depends on human effort. The authorities must not neglect it.

The Japanese Minister of War Inspects Osaka 24

Osaka—Minister of War Hayashi visited the headquarters of the Fourth Division yesterday and met with the Division Commander Prince Higashikuni to respond to various inquiries about important current military issues. At noon, he dined with the staff of the Division in the high-ranking officers' dining hall. The Division Commander also attended in person. Minister Hayashi then inspected the Sakai Regiment, the Osaka Army Airfield, etc. In the evening, he attended a banquet hosted by the Fourth Division. (Dentsu dispatch on the 26th)

Righteous Army of Liu Zhendong's Troops Gather Eight Hundred and Occupy Naiman Banner; Japanese-Puppet Allied Forces Dispatch Large Contingent; With Rising Green Crops, Bombing is Difficult 25

(Tokyo) The righteous army besieging Xing'an Naiman Banner is from the Liu Zhendong unit, with a strength of approximately eight hundred men. This morning at five o'clock, the Japanese air force stationed in Gongzhuling was ordered to dispatch. The cavalry unit stationed in Kailu and the Japanese garrison in Zhengjiatun also departed at five o'clock this morning. The vanguard, a police force of one hundred and fifty men from "Manchukuo," engaged in battle with the righteous army at ten o'clock this morning. Once the Japanese-Manchu allied forces arrive, a general offensive will commence. The "Manchu" and Mongolian Affairs Department convened a meeting this morning to discuss countermeasures, seeking the cause of the mutiny in order to fundamentally resolve the situation. (Hualian Telegram, 26th)

(Changchun) According to a telegram received by the Mongolian Affairs Department, the Liu Zhendong unit has completely occupied Naiman City and openly taken hostile actions against the Japanese army. The "Manchukuo" Gendarmerie and the Xing'an West Province Police Force launched a general offensive this morning with a small force of one hundred and fifty men. After fierce fighting, numerous casualties have occurred. However, the Liu Zhendong unit is resisting stubbornly, so the "Manchu" army is currently awaiting Japanese reinforcements. (Dentsu Telegram, 26th)

(Changchun) Yesterday, the Zhengjiatun Independent Garrison Unit, leading a machine gun unit, infantry unit, communications unit, and cavalry unit, departed to suppress the Liu Zhendong unit occupying the Naiman Brigade Public Office. (Dentsu Telegram, 26th)

(Changchun) According to a statement from the "Manchu" Military and Political Department authorities, the Xing'anling Flying Squadron, after reconnaissance of the Naiman Banner Public Office at seven o'clock this morning, has commenced suppression operations. Currently, the sorghum is lush, and out of concern for damaging the city streets of the banner, bombing has not been carried out. However, if the "bandits" resist stubbornly, bombing will be unavoidable. As for the Japanese who have been kidnapped, there is likely no hope for them. (Dentsu Telegram, 26th)

(Changchun) The Japanese and Mongolian Affairs Department authorities convened an emergency meeting at ten o'clock this morning regarding the follow-up measures for the Naiman Banner incident. The issue behind this incident involves the governance of both Mongolian and Manchu ethnicities in the Rehe Mongolian region. Therefore, it has a significant impact on the administrative direction of Manchukuo and is worthy of serious attention. (Dentsu Telegram, 26th)

(Changchun) According to a public announcement received by the Changchun Mongolian Affairs Department at four o'clock in the afternoon on the 25th, the purpose of the attack on the Naiman Banner Public Office was indeed to brutally massacre Japanese. Nakane and Tsuruta have already been killed in action, and other Japanese have been kidnapped, their fates unknown. Furthermore, the Japanese and Manchu armies have completed a complete encirclement of the "bandit" group. (Dentsu Telegram, 26th)

(Changchun) The following is a statement by Vice Minister Yoda of the Manchukuo Mongolian Affairs Department: Before the Manchurian Incident, "bandits" were already rampant in the Naiman Banner area. The situation has greatly improved after the Incident. Currently, security is mainly maintained by the Manchu police, and self-defense corps are organized to promote the autonomy of the Mongolian ethnicity. The reasons for the occurrence of this incident are: (1) The area was formerly known as Suidong County, and dissatisfaction arose after it was changed to a banner and incorporated into Inner Mongolia. (2) Councilor Yamamori secretly and strictly suppressed bandits, causing resentment. (Dentsu Telegram, 26th)

CER Russian Staff All Withdrawn to Home Country, Reaching 18,000 People 26

(Tokyo) The agreement for the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway (CER) stipulates that the deadline for the withdrawal of Soviet Railway Bureau staff is August 20th. After this date, all Red personnel within "Manchukuo" territory must be completely withdrawn to their home country. On the 26th, the Ambassador to Manchukuo, General Minami, reported to the Foreign Ministry that as of July 22nd, a total of 18,345 people have been completely withdrawn. Approximately 1,000 people have not yet completed the process. In addition, approximately 1,000 people who are not Railway Bureau staff are also seeking withdrawal. A total of 2,000 people are still staying in the territory and will be completely repatriated to the Soviet Union before August 20th. (Nichiren Telegram, 26th)

East African War Imminent, Abyssinia Appeals to League of Nations for Intervention, Urges Executive Council to Convene Meeting Swiftly, Italy's Delaying Tactic, Willing to Continue Arbitration, Rome Diplomatic Negotiations Make No Progress 27

(Geneva) League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol has received a note from the Abyssinian government, reiterating its request for the immediate convening of a League of Nations Executive Council meeting to address the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. The note states that due to the urgency of the situation, the League of Nations Executive Council should intervene immediately. The negotiations made by several countries to peacefully resolve the dispute will not be hindered by the intervention of the Executive Council. The resolution previously passed by the Executive Council stipulated that if the Italo-Abyssinian arbitration committee cannot reach a compromise by July 25th, the Executive Council should immediately convene a meeting to appoint a fifth neutral arbitrator. Currently, this deadline has passed, and the situation has not changed. After receiving this note, Avenol telegraphed all members attending the Executive Council in the afternoon. Once he receives replies from various countries, he can decide the date of the Executive Council meeting, which is expected to be around July 31st. (Havas Telegram, 26th)

(Geneva) Abyssinia today requested the League of Nations Executive Council to convene a meeting to find a way to avoid the East African war. Italy suddenly sent a telegram, signed by Undersecretary Suvich, stating its willingness to submit the Italo-Abyssinian dispute to arbitration negotiations. The Italian telegram arrived on the day the League of Nations' deadline for arbitration negotiations was about to expire. The telegram stated that Italy's previous opposition to arbitration was because the matters that Abyssinia requested to discuss were not within the scope of the League of Nations arbitration agreement. Italy sent two telegrams to the Abyssinian capital on July 14th and 23rd, urging Abyssinia to withdraw these requests so that the arbitration committee could continue its work. The League of Nations authorities are studying the telegrams from both Italy and Abyssinia in order to decide whether to immediately convene an Executive Council meeting and to determine whether arbitration negotiations can continue. (Guomin Telegram, 25th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Executive Council today asked Secretary-General Avenol to decide before tomorrow afternoon whether the meeting to consider the Italo-Abyssinian dispute should be held on July 30th or August 1st. The first task of the League of Nations Executive Council at the meeting will be to decide whether the scope of discussion should be limited to border conflicts or whether to consider the entire dispute. Avenol replied that the Executive Council members could decide on July 31st or August 1st. However, regardless of which day the meeting is held, it will begin at 5:00 PM. (Reuters Telegram, 26th)

(Rome) Attempts to peacefully resolve the Italo-Abyssinian dispute have made no progress after Undersecretary Suvich held talks with the British Ambassador to Italy yesterday. Yesterday, British Ambassador Drummond visited Undersecretary Suvich, claiming to discuss minor matters unrelated to the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. However, during the conversation, he still brought up the Abyssinian issue as an aside. Drummond did not put forward any new suggestions. Britain expressed its support for the compromise plan established last week (i.e., Italy would build a railway through Abyssinia in Italian Somaliland and Eritrea, and Abyssinia would grant Italy broad trade benefits as conditions for resolving the dispute). If this compromise plan cannot be established, it is decided to submit the issue to the League of Nations Executive Council for handling in its entirety. Also, during yesterday's mass rally in Rome to send off troops to East Africa, the masses held various insulting signs against Britain, which greatly angered the British expatriates in Italy. The disputes between Britain and Italy have therefore increased. As for France's efforts, its purpose is to support last week's compromise plan. According to the 1906 Anglo-Franco-Italian Treaty (i.e., if one of the signatory countries wants to intervene in the Abyssinian issue, it should first consult with the other countries), a conference of Britain, France, and Italy should be convened to resolve the dispute. France advocates expanding Italy's rights in Abyssinia, imitating the cooperation model between Britain and Iraq. On the one hand, Italy abandons its war against Abyssinia, and on the other hand, Britain makes broad concessions to Italy. However, given the current situation, this compromise plan seems unlikely to be realized, because the Italian newspapers continue to make anti-British remarks, and the tensions between Britain and Italy are high. The only outcome may be to submit the matter to the League of Nations Executive Council for handling. (Havas Telegram, 26th)

Italian Government Document Reopens Path to Mediation, Does Not Refuse to Send Representatives to Attend League of Nations Meeting 28

(Geneva) The Secretary-General of the League of Nations has released an Italian government document, which shows that Italy hopes that the League of Nations Executive Council will postpone its meeting to consider the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. The document states that the mediation and arbitration procedures were suspended entirely because the Abyssinian government's representatives in Sheveningen made requests and insisted that the committee discuss issues not included in the arbitration agreement. The Italian government now wishes to continue with these procedures to completion. At the same time, the League of Nations Executive Council has received a letter from the Abyssinian government stating that the League of Nations Executive Council should convene a meeting as soon as possible to consider the Abyssinian request made under Article 15 of the League of Nations Covenant. The Italian government document also states that the Italian government has notified the Abyssinian government that it is willing to have the committee reconvene in accordance with the scope of the arbitration committee agreement to mediate the disputes between the two countries, and asks the Abyssinian government to withdraw its previous requests so that the committee can continue its work. Geneva sees this Italian document as indicating that the Italian government believes that mediation has not yet reached a dead end. The document implies that the Italian government will limit the discussions in Geneva to border conflicts and conditions for mediators to refer to, and that the League of Nations Executive Council will be allowed to propose the appointment of a fifth arbitrator. This policy conforms to the government's views and will postpone the general discussion of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute by one month. However, it is still doubtful whether the Abyssinian representatives agree to this procedure. According to opinions within the League of Nations, the Italian government document has actually reopened the path to mediation. If the Abyssinian government's reply agrees, the deadline for negotiations will be extended to August 25th. If so, the issue of the League of Nations Executive Council meeting next week will be void. If the Abyssinian government's reply refuses, the Executive Council will meet as scheduled. Most people expect the Abyssinian government to refuse. However, in any case, the Italian government will obviously try its best to limit the discussion of the Executive Council meeting to mediation issues. (Reuters Telegram, 26th)

(Rome) Regarding the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, Italy believes that it can now obtain a solution that can be accepted by the country. Therefore, the country does not have to withdraw from the League of Nations and can obtain freedom of action in East Africa. Italian government officials believe that Japan's actions in the four northeastern provinces of China in the past, although criticized, are not as serious as the current Italo-Abyssinian dispute. Italian public opinion has recently eased because the British Cabinet refused to issue export licenses for military supplies to Abyssinia. The British government has now decided to send Minister without Portfolio Eden to Geneva to attend the extraordinary meeting of the League of Nations Executive Council, and has reportedly ordered him to adopt a moderate attitude. (Havas Telegram, 26th)

(Rome) According to Italian semi-official sources, Italy does not recognize the League of Nations' right to fully discuss the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, believing that the Italo-Abyssinian Treaty was signed after Italy and Abyssinia joined the League of Nations. Therefore, the procedures contained in the Italo-Abyssinian Treaty should be applied to disputes between the two countries, and not the procedures of the League of Nations Covenant. As for the present, Italy does not refuse to send representatives to Geneva to attend the meeting of the League of Nations Executive Council. However, if the methods passed by the Executive Council to handle the Italo-Abyssinian dispute are contrary to Italy's claims, Italy will withdraw from the League of Nations and withdraw its representatives from the League of Nations. (Havas Telegram, 25th)

France Faces Dilemma, Must Consider Both Anglo-Italian Friendship, Laval to Personally Go to Geneva 29

(Paris) According to official sources, the League of Nations Executive Council has scheduled a meeting on the 31st of this month to discuss the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. France has not yet adopted a definite attitude towards this dispute. It is reported that on the one hand, the government will try to avoid hindering friendly relations between France, Britain, and Italy, and on the other hand, it will strive to adhere to the various principles of the League of Nations. (Havas Telegram, 25th)

(Paris) According to well-informed officials, Prime Minister Laval has a lot of administrative affairs, but he has still decided to go to Geneva on Monday and intends to propose a plan based on the 1906 treaty, making Abyssinia a protectorate of Italy. This proposal also stipulates that the area around Lake Tsana is within the British sphere of influence. Italy exchanged notes in December 1925, recognizing Britain's full right to handle the lake. (Guomin Telegram, 25th)

100,000 Italian Citizens Demonstrate Against Britain, Abyssinia, and Japan, Holding Up Banners to Send Off Expeditionary Forces 30

(Rome) Last night, 100,000 Roman citizens gathered in front of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to express their loyalty to Prime Minister Mussolini and to show that Mussolini can obtain the full assistance of the people in the dispute with Abyssinia. Demonstrators carried various flags expressing hatred for Abyssinia, Britain, and Japan. This was aroused by a long-standing propaganda campaign by Italian newspapers. One flag depicted a Fascist Party member holding an axe and splitting a flag with a cross of Britain and Japan. Another flag depicted the Abyssinian King hanging upside down by his trousers. Demonstrators shouted "Down with Abyssinia!", "Down with Britain!", "Down with Japan!" The cries were echoed by tens of thousands of people, shaking the streets. The Fascist Youth League sang revolutionary songs, interspersed with shouts against Britain, Abyssinia, and Japan. The League of Nations was also subjected to venomous slander. Huge posters were pasted all over the streets, alluding to the three countries of Britain, Abyssinia, and Japan. Under the posters were slogans saying, "Rome will preserve Europe, we must win!" There were also brown posters depicting Europeans, Japanese, and Filipinos having friendly relations, and Abyssinia selling slaves. The slogans occasionally included the cry of "Malta! Malta!" General Starace, the Secretary of the Fascist Party, gave a speech to the crowd on the platform, demanding the opening up of territories for Italy. Similar gatherings were held in major cities across the country. Given the public's resentment towards Britain and Japan, the authorities have dispatched special guards to strictly protect the British and Japanese embassies. At the same time, the diplomatic circles of France, Britain, and Italy are also very active. Italian Prime Minister Mussolini has moved to his residence at the Rocca delle Caminate castle. Mussolini goes there whenever he makes important decisions. Emergency documents are now being sent there daily for review. Last night, a large ship departed from Liverpool for East Africa, carrying 1,000 machine gunners, who were disbanded from the Italian army's cavalry. (Reuters, 26th)

(Rome) A demonstration was held here to send off troops to East Africa, initiated by various Fascist Party groups. At 10:00 PM, they gathered at the Piazza Colonna in front of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, each holding a sign saying that Italy should maintain freedom of action and not be bound by world public opinion, and that the firm will of the Italian nation cannot be hindered by anything. Fanziogli Gracci, the General Secretary of the Fascist Party, gave a passionate speech, saying that the war against Abyssinia can be won, and we should all sacrifice ourselves for the country. (Havas Telegram, 25th)

Italy's War Preparations in Full Swing, Soldiers, Supplies, and Arms Continuously Transported to Africa, 40,000 Officers Undergoing Strict Training 31

(Rome) Italy continues to prepare for war on a large scale today. Troops, supplies, and arms are being concentrated throughout the country, and soldiers and military supplies are being continuously transported to East Africa. According to news here today, 40,000 officers are currently undergoing strict training, so that after the mobilization of the 1915 and 1916 classes, 500,000 troops can have commanders. According to Italy's military plan, 1.7 million people can be mobilized within two months. (Guomin Telegram, 25th)

The Italian steamship Count Biancamano departed from Naples last night, carrying 1,100 machine gun unit soldiers, 30 officers, 800 colonial army soldiers, 150 officers, and 600 specialized workers, as well as a large quantity of military equipment. When the ship arrived at Beishina Port, another 580 soldiers and 21 officers boarded the ship there. In total, the ship carried more than 200 officers and more than 3,000 soldiers, who will go to Mogadishu in Africa. When the ship departed from here last night, a large number of people gathered at the pier to send them off, the situation was extremely enthusiastic. (Havas Telegram, 26th)

Abyssinian King States, Vows to Live and Die With Soldiers, Says Italian Army Has Ways to Fail 32

(Paris) The Abyssinian Emperor, in an interview with a special correspondent of "Paris Evening News," stated, "I have always trusted the resolutions that the League of Nations can make, especially if Britain and France can uphold justice and join Abyssinia's side, then I should trust them even more. However, it is impossible to make any territorial or economic concessions to Italy. If the two countries declare war, I should first serve on the battlefield and live and die with the soldiers. As for the Italian army, it is very likely to fail. Firstly, the Italian army is separated by Italian Somaliland on one side and British Somaliland on the other, making communication very inconvenient. Secondly, it will encounter endless difficulties fighting in the high mountains. Thirdly, there is a complete lack of drinking water in the Gorden Desert, making it inconvenient to march. Fourthly, there will be many deserters from the indigenous troops of Italian Somaliland and Eritrea. These are all ways for Italy to fail." The Abyssinian Emperor then lamented that various countries have banned the transport of military supplies to Abyssinia, and that the contracts for the purchase of military supplies signed by Belgium, Czechoslovakia, and the United States have all been cancelled. (Havas Telegram, 26th)

Invention of Heavy Oil Production from Coal, A Major Revolution in Japanese Heavy Industry 37

(Tokyo) Dr. Isobe of the Institute of Physical and Chemical Research has been researching the liquefaction of coal for the past ten years. As a result of the invention of this method, each ton of coal costing ten yuan can be used to produce a ton of heavy oil worth forty yuan, which is a major revolution in heavy industry. Chinese Antiques Transported to Britain, Stored in Burlington House, British Newspapers Greatly Praise the Greatness of Chinese Art 38

(London) Employees of Burlington House found this morning when they arrived at the building that the 18-foot-high iron gate had been locked, the first time this has happened in many years. There were many armed guards in the courtyard protecting the trucks carrying Chinese antiques. After 9:00 AM, the gate was opened, and a truck drove to the side of Burlington House, after which the gate was closed again. The boxes were then successively transported into the warehouse to await unpacking. Great care was taken when unloading, for fear of damaging the antiques. This work was supervised by Zheng Tiansi. (Reuters Telegram, 26th)

(London) Now that the British warship Suffolk has transported Chinese antiques to England, its captain, Manners, has been promoted to rear admiral. He has requested to retire due to old age. Many newspapers have commented on the arrival of Chinese antiques in England, which is very beneficial to the promotion of the exhibition. The Times stated that the beauty of the exhibits will certainly fill and exceed the excitement that has already arisen. The timing of this exhibition is quite good, because due to the cultivation of Lawrence Binyon and other scholars of Eastern art, the general public has recently become deeply aware of the greatness of Chinese art. Chinese artists are respected by the world, unlike some later Eastern artists who are jealous and afraid of them and impose their needs to exclude others' strengths by being arrogant. It would be a pleasure if Western art continued to be influenced by Chinese art in what it urgently needs. Will these ninety-three boxes of Chinese art exhibit their strange power here? The Morning Post stated that Chinese works of art have now arrived safely in England. No ship that has come to England has ever carried items of greater value than this. Britain has been using Burlington House as a place for winter exhibitions of the art of a country for many years, and it has become a very good habit. Masterpieces of Italy, France, Belgium, Holland, and Persia have been appreciated by London. Now, thanks to the generosity of the Chinese government, England can appreciate some of Chinese art. Perhaps the exhibits can be poetic material for the vagaries of the world. (Reuters Telegram, 26th)

Opening of the Third International Congress. More than 600 Representatives from 65 Countries. Future Work will Maintain Liberal Democratic Governance. 40

Ministry of Finance Announces Rules of Procedure for Liquidation Commissioners of Closed Banks and Firms 43

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance announced on the 27th eight articles of the Rules of Procedure for Liquidation Commissioners supervising the liquidation of closed banks and firms, stipulating the powers and duties of the commissioners: 1. Reviewing various accounting statements; 2. Inspecting capital; 3. Reviewing the sale or disposal of movable and immovable property; 4. Reviewing the receipt and payment of liquidation funds; 5. Implementing orders from the Ministry of Finance and investigating and responding to various matters. In order to perform their duties, commissioners may inquire with relevant responsible personnel at any time and direct operations. If the responsible personnel evade, conceal, or intentionally delay matters, the commissioner may report to the Ministry of Finance for disciplinary action. When necessary, commissioners may go to the relevant banks and money houses and branches to supervise liquidation. (Special Dispatch of the 26th)

French Craftsman Creates a "Flying Locust" a Small Airplane that Costs Only 10,000 Francs, with a Simple Structure and Wings that Can Retract into the Fuselage. 89

(Paris) A carpenter named Milian here has ingeniously created a small airplane with an engine power of 25 horsepower, costing only 10,000 francs. After completion, it was named "Flying Locust". It is estimated that up to 10,000 units can be manufactured within a year. The advantage of this aircraft is its simple structure. The two wings are installed on the same horizontal plane in front and behind the fuselage. The wings are fully extended during flight, and when it reaches maximum speed, the ends of both wings can be retracted into the fuselage. Thus, the width of the wings is reduced by one-third, and the air resistance is reduced accordingly, and the speed will naturally increase. When landing, simply extend the wings to gradually reduce the speed. This method was invented by a Russian immigrant named Makunin and has recently been approved by the Ministry of Aviation. Currently, the enthusiasm for promoting the "Flying Locust" throughout France is comparable to Germany's promotion of gliding. (Havas News Agency Telegram of the 26th)

Gold and Silver

The price of gold in London today was 14 shillings and 6.5 pence, down 2 pence.

The silver market in Mumbai today opened lower and the market was quiet, but it stabilized at the close. The spot price was 70 rupees and 8 annas, down 1 anna. The futures price also fell 1 anna to 70 rupees and 13 annas and 71 rupees and 3 annas.

Silver futures in Mountrie were quite quiet today. The September contract opened down 10 pounds, at 67.95 to 68.25.

New York Commodity Market Prices

Inspection Report on Flood Conditions Along the Rivers, Special Correspondent Geng Ya of This Newspaper 90

Visit to the Disaster Areas of Zhang Gong Embankment and Jinyintan

Hankou is situated at the confluence of the Yangtze and Han rivers. It is bordered by the Yangtze River in the front, and the Xiang River and Yu Lake in the back. The embankments along the rivers, including the Zhang Gong Embankment, encircle the city like a crescent moon, spanning eighty or ninety li in length. Outside the embankment, the vast expanse of water has transformed into a marshland. Inside, the terrain is low-lying, with the water level reaching about ten feet higher. During the 1931 Zhang Gong Embankment breach, the city of Hankou was flooded to a depth of several feet. This time, despite minor leaks, the embankment was successfully defended due to effective precautions, avoiding a repeat of the disaster from twenty years ago. As I awaited the ship heading further up the Yangtze River, I decided to conduct an inspection of the Zhang Gong Embankment.

On the 25th, I set off by car at five in the morning. As the urban landscape of the Pinghan Railway faded into the distance, the rural scenery came into view. The roadside was adorned with golden rice paddies and white lotus flowers, their fragrant aroma permeating the air. Bathed in the morning sun, I felt as if I were cleansing my spirit in an ice urn. Before we had traveled fifteen li, the sounds of laboring and the scent of sweat from the embankment workers at Gusushu greeted us. Gusushu is a small town nestled against the embankment, crowded with embankment workers and refugees, creating a bustling scene. Several days ago, the inner slope of the nearby embankment suddenly began to sink into the lotus swamp. Immediate rescue efforts were launched around the clock. Due to the high water level in Moon Lake outside the embankment and the low-lying terrain inside, it was impossible to resist the water's force. As a result, the pilings shifted, and the soil subsided. Five rows of large pilings were driven in, but they all gradually moved and collapsed into the lotus swamp along with the surrounding soil. Fortunately, the water receded by five or six feet, allowing them to narrowly avert disaster. However, the work of driving pilings and pressing soil continues day and night, proceeding actively.

The area along the embankment is covered with reed and straw sheds, serving as offices for the "Jianghan Engineering Bureau," the "Flood Prevention Association," and the "Ordnance Factory." They also serve as places where the "Good Deeds Association," the "Municipal Health Department," the "Municipal Oil Industry Association," and various charitable organizations provide tea, medicine, and steamed buns. Other areas serve as storage for engineering materials such as burlap sacks, reed mats, bamboo, wood, and hemp rope. Most of the male workers are engaged in driving pilings and building earthworks, working in groups of dozens, their voices echoing for miles. Women carry soil and transport materials, tirelessly working back and forth. Plainclothes soldiers and supervisory personnel, often armed with long bamboo poles, direct the work and maintain order. Small snack vendors have also set up stalls along the roadside, creating a lively atmosphere reminiscent of a rural market. However, a closer look at the faces of those present reveals an unspoken inner anxiety, which the tense atmosphere of fighting the raging floodwaters cannot completely conceal. This is because the safety and well-being of Hankou's eight hundred thousand residents and their property depend on whether this embankment can be effectively defended.

Flooded Scenery on the Riverside Road of Hankou

Traveling downstream along the embankment for about seven or eight li, we encountered more than twenty workers repairing leaks. The soil needed for the repairs had to be dug from the opposite bank of the lotus swamp, making transportation by boat inconvenient. The inner slope of the embankment was covered in lush green grass, with herds of cattle grazing. In the distance, the fields were golden with grain, and the cotton was in bloom, suggesting the promise of a bountiful harvest. However, to the left, the raging waves crashed against the embankment with a deafening roar. Villages such as Jinyintan, Qijiatun, Xingjiatun, and Zhangjiatun had all been submerged, transformed into underwater palaces. Crops had been washed away, and villagers had sought refuge on the embankment, erecting makeshift shelters with reed mats and digging holes for stoves, barely able to escape the wind and rain and eke out a living.

Jinyintan is only a li or two away from the embankment. The collapsed walls and standing pillars, along with the tree branches brushing against the water, were clearly visible. We hired a boat to cross over, and the depth of the water felt considerable. The boatman tested the depth with an oar, revealing it to be more than fifteen feet deep. We first reached Jintan, where only a few dozen roof tiles remained visible. Everywhere else was water. One family, surnamed Yang, had a house on slightly higher ground, and the water had receded from their courtyard. The owner was sweeping away the silt, preparing to return home. When asked, "The water hasn't completely receded, why are you rushing back?" he replied, "The reed shed on the embankment only provides minimal shelter from the sun. If it rains at night, we will still be drenched." When asked about the living conditions of the villagers, he replied, "On the night of July 11th, the floodwaters came fiercely, initially rising by a foot or so. By dawn, the water had entered our homes, rising steadily by five or six feet. Jintan has about 170 households, and Yintan has 110. The cries of despair shook the fields like an earthquake. In a panic, everyone grabbed small boats and wooden objects, risking their lives to float to the embankment. The wheat had just been harvested, and the melons were ripe but not yet picked. Everyone was too busy trying to save their lives to worry about the melons and wheat. For the past half-month, the flood victims have been relying on duckweed (floating plants), water chestnut leaves (i.e., water chestnut leaves), and wheat bran for food, but even these are becoming scarce. If benevolent people don't come to our rescue, the flood victims will soon turn into starving corpses on land." The owner had a son, twelve or thirteen years old, who was studying at a primary school in Huangpi. He was also present and pointed out the watermarks on the remaining walls, measuring them with his height, appearing lively and adorable. The owner sighed and said, "This child would have graduated in a year, and his grades are not bad, but he will have to drop out of school from now on. What a pity!" The boy, hearing this, forced a smile, but his innocent heart could not contain his tears, which welled up in his eyes.

We then boated to Yintan, where the scene was similar to Jintan. However, Yintan had also suffered a fire on April 11th, making the lives of the villagers even more miserable. Ashore, we saw an old woman leading her granddaughters, their feet covered in mud and their hair disheveled, salvaging what remained of their belongings that had not been washed away. Upon seeing the reporter, she mistook me for a disaster relief worker and stumbled forward through the mud to greet me, wiping away tears with the corner of her shirt. Knowing what she wanted, I was thinking of how to comfort her when she suddenly slipped and fell in the mud. I rushed forward to help her up, and her granddaughters also ran over. The old woman lamented, crying and saying, "Yintan has suffered both flood and fire within a hundred days. The common people are truly cursed. But the officials don't allow us to perform operas for the gods, which is also a mistake. The water rose more than ten feet high overnight. What else could it be but divine water? Alas, truly cursed, truly cursed." After comforting her, I entered a relatively intact house. I saw a bed turned upside down on the central beam, with miscellaneous items and wooden puppets stored on it. A dead dog was tied to a pillar in the courtyard, already smelling foul. The owner must have fled in a hurry, forgetting to untie it, leading to its death. On the way back by boat, the boatman suddenly asked, "Is Zhang Xueliang the son of Zhang Zhidong?" Amused by his question, I asked, "Why do you ask?" He replied, "This Zhang Gong Embankment was built by Zhang Zhidong. When the floodwaters rose, a blue dragon was seen baring its teeth and claws in the lake by a member of the Zhang family. It is said that a god opera will be performed in Gusushu for three days starting on the 28th, and then the dragon will ascend and the water will recede. If Zhang is truly the son of Zhang Gong, we can hope that floods will be reduced in the future." It is unexpected that ignorant people constantly attribute fortune and misfortune to fate. After a major disaster, there are even more far-fetched superstitious claims. While their feelings are understandable, it also reveals the shortcomings of a lack of education.

After passing through Shanlishan, Danshuichi, Fenjinlu, and other places, we bypassed the Japanese concession's riverside embankment. At first, I did not realize it was the Japanese concession until I saw many sandbags piled up along the riverside road. The wind and waves outside the embankment also seemed stronger than near the Jianghan Customs House. I was about to take a photo when I saw a sign next to the sandbag pile that read "Freedom of Entry and Exit." Realizing where I was because of the different wording, I first informed the Indian police officer, who shook his head and stopped me. Passing between wharves 2 and 3 in Special District 3, I saw more than ten workers bathing naked outside the embankment on Linjiang Road. A patrolman suddenly jumped out from inside the embankment, grabbed their clothes, and left. These people recklessly enjoyed the convenience of bathing in the river and suffered this blow. It could be said that they gained less than they lost.

Zhang Gong Embankment Repair Situation

Crossing the river, I visited Mr. Feng Ruofei and Mr. Deng Hejiu, secretaries of the provincial government. According to them, "This time, the flood in Hubei Province has caused fifty or sixty embankment breaches and around five hundred polder breaches. The area and population affected by the disaster have not yet been statistically determined. According to estimates from the counties reporting disasters, only one or two cotton-producing counties remain in the entire province, and the loss of cotton harvest is estimated to be over 100 million yuan. The loss of provincial business tax revenue will also reach 600,000 to 700,000 yuan. A total of forty-nine locations have reported disasters. Although these are not all counties, they are all key areas. Hanchuan and Tianmen are still submerged. The water is gradually receding in more than half of the remaining areas. However, 12 million yuan is needed for emergency, agricultural, industrial, and relief funds, and only over 400,000 yuan has been raised, which is less than one-tenth of the plan. We urgently hope that the central government and people from all walks of life will provide strong support." They also said, "Although the disaster situation in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River is severe, it is not as bad as that in the Xiang River basin. The water level in the Yangtze River basin, such as in the severely affected areas of Jingmen and Yichang, has gradually receded. However, many counties in the Xiang River basin are still suffering in deep water and scorching heat. To inspect the situation, we should first choose counties in the Xiang River basin. However, transportation is inconvenient, and the journey is much more arduous than traveling by Yangtze River steamer." Therefore, I decided to inspect Xiangcheng first and planned to depart on the 26th. If the roads are clear, I may take the Xiangxianghua Road and then take the Pinghan train north to investigate the Yellow River disaster.

Emergency Construction of the Great Embankment in Northern Jiangsu 91

Reasons Why Yellow River Water Has Not Immediately Flooded Weishan Lake; Major Construction of the Great Embankment is Nearing Completion

Xuzhou Correspondence: Following the Yellow River breach in Western Shandong, the Yellow River water flowed into Nanyang Lake. Because the terrain between Nanyang Lake and Weishan Lake is relatively high, and there is no continuous major flow of water, the Yellow River water has not yet flooded Weishan Lake. Xia Town, located on the northern bank of Weishan Lake and connected to the Central Canal, has also not seen any Yellow River water. However, because the lakes between Northern Jiangsu and Southern Shandong are interconnected, and there have been heavy rains in recent days, the water level has risen slightly. Inspector Ding Chaowu, Commissioner Shao Hanyuan, and Committee Member Lan Weibin traveled by steamship to the banks of Weishan Lake on the 24th to inspect the situation and supervise the embankment construction. Engineer Yu Shufang, specially dispatched by the Construction Department, also went from Pei County to Xia Town on the 24th to inspect the area and set up water gauges to confirm that the water from Nanyang Lake was overflowing northward. Therefore, the water has not yet flooded into the counties under the jurisdiction of Northern Jiangsu and Xuzhou. Currently, they are busy constructing the Great Embankment of Northern Jiangsu and the Lianjia Dam Embankment, as well as inspecting the canal locks. Technicians from the counties bordering Shandong, Anhui, and the counties under the jurisdiction of Xuzhou have been gathering in Xuzhou in recent days for inspection. Due to differing interests, they have different views on the embankment construction. Ding, Shao, and Lan all believe that the Great Embankment of Northern Jiangsu should be completed as soon as possible, while the Lianjia Dam Embankment requires further inspection before a decision can be made. The Provincial Governor has not been able to attend to the water conservancy issues in Jiangbei in the past, and now should thoroughly plan for them.

Overflowing Water from Nanyang Lake

The Yellow River water flowing south from the breach at Linpu is divided into two streams that flow into Nanyang Lake. One stream enters Zhaowang River via Juye and flows into Dushan Lake to flood Nanyang Lake. The other stream enters Niutou River via Jiaxiang to flood Nanyang Lake. The two streams are competing, so the water in Nanyang Lake is rising rapidly. Because the terrain between Nanyang Lake and Weishan Lake is relatively high, the lake water overflows northward. Part of the water floods towards Jining, and part of the water enters Yutai. Currently, postal and telecommunications between Yutai and Jining have been cut off. Yutai's southern border is adjacent to Feng and Pei counties, which are under the jurisdiction of Xuzhou. Feng County sent Peng Shiting and Huang Tirun to inspect the Nanyang Lake area near Yutai a few days ago. The Yuanwa Lake dam in the northeast of Yutai has a breach of over 20 zhang. The Fifth District of Yutai is severely affected by the disaster. There is an old dam along the lake, starting from the northwest at Yuanwa and extending southeast to Chengzi Temple in Pei County, for a length of over 80 li. Yutai is currently conscripting laborers to repair the dam. Because of this overflow of water from Nanyang Lake, the water has not been able to flood Weishan Lake. Therefore, when Ding, Lan, and others inspected the area yesterday, the water level was still stable. Xia Town is located on the northern border of Pei County, on the northern bank of Weishan Lake. It is an important passage connecting the lake to the canal. In the past, before the canal transport was abolished, it was an important area. Pei County has set up a water gauge here. Engineer Yu went to inspect the area yesterday and did not see any Yellow River water. If there are no more major floods, then Northern Jiangsu may be spared from the water disaster. However, according to Engineers Zhou Yushan and Zhao Yusu, who were sent to Shandong by the Construction Department and the Huai River Conservancy Committee to inspect the breach, they returned to Xuzhou and reported that they inspected the breach at Linpu on the 20th. There were a total of six breaches. The first two breaches have silted up. The third and fourth breaches have very little water flow. The fifth breach is the largest, with a length of 300 meters. The sixth breach is the next largest, with a length of 120 meters. The distance between the fifth and sixth breaches is about 800 meters. The water flow is strong in both breaches. When inspecting the area, it took three hours to travel five li upstream by boat and only half an hour to travel downstream. Moreover, if a major flood continues, it may even wash away the remaining dam between the fifth and sixth breaches, and the two breaches may merge into one, then the water situation will be uncontrollable. Zhang Lianjia, Director of the Shandong River Affairs Bureau, is monitoring the breach and plans to carry out willow plugging work, but it is unknown whether it will be effective.

The Great Embankment of Northern Jiangsu

The counties under the jurisdiction of Xuzhou view the Great Embankment of Northern Jiangsu as a safeguard for the northwestern half of the region. However, it is by no means intended to stop the Yellow River water from diverting the canal. The embankment starts from Chengzi Temple in northern Pei County, connects to the old dam in Lutai in the north, and extends to Fangcun in northern Tong County in the south, close to the Yunkou Lock. The Yutai Embankment borders the west bank of Nanyang Port and is intended to prevent the westward flooding of Nanyang Lake. The embankment borders the west bank of Weishan Lake and is intended to prevent the westward overflow of Weishan Lake water. If the Yellow River water enters Weishan Lake, it will inevitably divert the canal. If it is unavoidable, the water can only be allowed to enter the canal from the southeastern bank of the lake. It must not be allowed to overflow to the southwestern bank. Therefore, the construction of this embankment is intended to prevent the flooding of Weishan Lake and serve as a barrier for the northeastern border of Feng, Pei, Xiao, Dang, and Tong counties. It has nothing to do with the Yellow River changing its course and diverting the canal. The Yunkou Lock is indeed related to the connection between Weishan Lake and the canal. However, it is a lock and not an embankment. In the past, during canal transport, the water in Weishan Canal was regulated by the lock. The provincial government and the counties along the canal all advocate for its repair, as the lock is the key to Weishan Canal. The canal has been in disrepair for a long time, and if a large amount of water is suddenly released, the canal will not be able to accommodate it. With a lock and a dam, the canal can be maintained. At the same time, the embankments along the canal are also being repaired urgently. However, a thorough overhaul of the canal would involve a large project and would have to wait for a later date. The counties along the canal hope that the provincial government will be able to repair the canal as soon as possible, so as to avoid being caught off guard in emergencies. Engineers Zhou Yushan and Zhao Yusu went to Hanzhuang yesterday morning to inspect the Yunkou Lock. They returned to the provincial capital by train last night from Hanzhuang. It is likely that the provincial government will formulate plans for reorganization after the two engineers submit their reports on the Yunkou Lock. Zhang Shuchun, a technician from Teng County, was sent to Xuzhou by the Shandong Construction Department to investigate the relationship between the Great Embankment of Northern Jiangsu and the Yunkou Lock. He conducted a thorough investigation and seemed to hold dissenting opinions regarding the construction of the embankment and the repair of the lock. After the investigation, he may be persuaded.

Inspection of Lianjia Dam

Lianjia Dam is located in the northern part of Tongshan County, south of Zhanggushan. It is the main lock and dam connecting to Weishan Lake. The southern bank of Weishan Lake is separated by a narrow strip of water, connecting to Zhanggushan. The water flows south through Zhanggushan to Lianjia Dam, where there are two rivers, the old and the new. One flows east, and the other flows south and then east, merging back into one to form the Bulao River, which enters the central canal of Pi County. This is the main river in northern Tong County. The Tongshan County Government has been ordered to repair the lock and build the dam. Although it is located in Tong County, it has a related impact on the counties to the east and west of Xuzhou. Recently, the heads of the construction departments and technicians of various counties, including Liao Chengzhang of Dangshan, Yuan Fengpan of Xiao County, and He Shiliang of Suining, have been transferred to Xuzhou by the special commissioner to engage in Yellow River flood control technical work. The counties have different views on the locks and dams in Lianjia Dam. The counties to the west of Xuzhou mainly focus on leading the water downstream to prevent backflow in the event of a breach. The counties to the east of Xuzhou mainly focus on preventing the water from flowing east and changing the embankment to cut off its flow. The construction of the Great Embankment of Weishan Lake has left culverts at the river mouths connecting Tong and Pei counties, with locks set up to store and discharge water, not just blocking the water in one way. The Tong County Government convened a meeting with representatives from all sectors yesterday and decided that Liu Xinyuan, head of the construction department, and representatives will go to Lianjia Dam this morning by car to conduct an on-site inspection, assess the situation, and then determine the construction methods. Generally speaking, repairing the dam and setting up the lock to control the opening and closing of the dam, and then dredging the Bulao River after the Yellow River flood control work is completed, is a predetermined and inevitable step, and also a comprehensive plan for water conservancy in northern Tong County. Tongshan is located directly north of Suxian County in Anhui Province. A technician from Suxian County was sent to Xuzhou a few days ago to investigate the Yellow River flooding and expressed sympathy for the Yellow River flood control facilities in the counties under the jurisdiction of Xuzhou and Tongshan. The interests of Xuzhou and Anhui are consistent, and Tong and Su are particularly close, and have decided to assist each other.

Comforting the Residents Building the Embankment

The Tongshan County Party Department and County Government have held several Yellow River flood control meetings and established a Yellow River Flood Control Coordination Association, with committee members from various agencies, construction committees, and local gentry. They have expressed their condolences to the residents building the embankment. A few days ago, the Tong County Party Department collected donations from all sectors and appointed representatives to go to the northern Tongshan and Weishan Lake coast this morning by car to provide comfort. County Magistrate Wang Gongying has been supervising the construction work on the Weishan Lake coast since the construction of the embankment began. After the representatives expressed their condolences, they inspected the Weishan Lake coast. The embankment has completed most of the project. The laborers have been working tirelessly under the scorching sun or in torrential rain. Magistrate Wang's face is covered with dust and his feet are covered in yellow mud. The residents call him the Chief Engineer. It is said that the embankment project can be completed on schedule (25th).

Jiang Song

Patrol Police Catch a Criminal Carrying Soil

Ma Wenguang, a detective from the Sixth Police Station of the Xin Zhuang Public Security Bureau, and police officer Wu Xuewen, while patrolling near the east side of the Xin Zhuang train station at around 2:00 a.m. on the 26th, noticed a suspicious pedestrian. When questioned, the person appeared flustered. As the officers attempted to search him, the pedestrian, relying on his strength, tried to punch the officers and escape. Fortunately, the military police stationed at the station heard the commotion and rushed over to help subdue him. They found 27 taels of secretly transported soil from Qia Ji hidden in his belt. He confessed that his name was Zhang Yushan, from Jinan, Shandong Province, and he lived on New Tokyo Road in the British Concession of Shanghai, where he ran the Yi He Da Bing shop. He was traveling to Songjiang to meet a fellow villager who ran a pancake stall there. Also, at around 1:00 p.m. on the 26th, detective Shen Zaihua of the Public Security Bureau saw a well-dressed pedestrian holding a "Beautiful" brand cigarette tin in front of the Quan Da Pawnshop on Dajie. When the pedestrian saw Officer Shen, he entered the pawnshop, arousing suspicion. Upon searching him, they found one tael of smuggled soil and half a tin of cigarette ash in the cigarette tin. Both cases have been handed over to the bureau for investigation and handling.

Suzhou

Merchants Petition Against Store Closures

Shops on Daogian Street and Yangyu Lane in the western part of the city have been greatly affected by the county government's construction of a small vegetable market in the Xiliku area, which forced all vegetable vendors to move into the market. To alleviate the impact, the shops jointly invested in establishing the Minsheng Vegetarian Food Store. However, the county government deemed this to be in violation of vegetable market regulations and sealed the store. The shops staged a strike to protest, but to no avail. Zhang Linsheng, the manager of the Minsheng Vegetarian Food Store, believes that the county government's closure was illegal and has expressed his dissatisfaction. He has submitted a petition to the county Party department seeking relief and also filed an administrative appeal with the provincial government on the 26th.

Provincial Committee Inspects the Demolition of Enclosures in Taihu Lake

The lake fields enclosed by residents from other provinces in Eastern Taihu Lake, located within the borders of Wu County, have been demolished through the joint efforts of the military and civilians. Gu Jiaoruo of the Provincial Committee, together with the Wu County Magistrate and the Nie Detachment Commander, traveled by boat to Eastern Taihu Lake on the 25th to inspect the demolition project. The results of the inspection were very satisfactory. When they returned to the Hengjing District Office at noon that day, hundreds of villagers blocked the road to petition for: (1) the petitioning committee to instruct Wujiang County to demolish all 70 shares of enclosed fields; (2) strict punishment of the 14 rioters who have been apprehended; (3) the dispatch of troops to disperse the residents from other provinces. Committee Member Gu agreed, and the villagers left satisfied. Shortly thereafter, Committee Member Gu notified Xu, the Magistrate of Wujiang County, by telephone to quickly demolish the 70 shares of enclosed fields to appease public opinion. Magistrate Xu replied that he would execute the order after receiving instructions from the province. Committee Member Gu and others returned to Suzhou at around 5:00 p.m. Committee Member Gu went to Wujiang County on the morning of the 26th to discuss the demolition of the 70 shares of enclosed fields with Magistrate Xu. He will return to Suzhou that evening.

Wuxi

Tea Houses Petition to Abolish the Tea Tax

The local Tea House Trade Association has previously submitted requests to the Jiangsu Provincial Tax Supervision Committee and other agencies, seeking the abolition of the tea tax, as they were already bearing four types of taxes: business tax, property tax, tea house tax, and public security license tax. They found the tax burden unbearable. Zhejiang Province abolished the tax in October last year, and Suzhou, Jiading, Nanxiang, and other counties in this province have also abolished it. However, this county is the only one that retains the old tax. Therefore, they have sent another letter to Zhang Peng, a member of the Jiangsu Provincial Tax Supervision Committee, requesting him to make a prompt decision, implement the original intention, alleviate the suffering of the people, and abolish the heavy taxes and abuses.

Changzhou

Case of Rape and Murder Near Banshang

Zhao Jin, a resident of Zhoujiaqiao Village near Banshang Town in the Sixth District of the county, had a son named Fu Lin, aged 28, who worked as a farmer. Several years ago, he married a woman named Zhang through a matchmaker. Zhang was of dissolute nature and had an affair with Zhao Arong, a neighbor. Unfortunately, their secret was discovered by Fu Lin's mother. Wishing to avoid public scandal, she gently tried to persuade them to stop. However, Zhang not only did not repent but also colluded with her lover, Zhao Arong, to beat her mother-in-law severely, pouring urine and feces on her, causing her to die. When her son returned home, she had already passed away. He reported the incident to the Sixth District Office, who then reported it to the local court for investigation. Prosecutor Guan Junjie led officials to the village on the 25th and found that the corpse had injuries all over its body, with clear marks of forceful pressure on the face. He determined that she had been beaten and suffocated to death before her death. The perpetrator, Zhao Arong, had fled. Prosecutor Guan ordered the parties involved and neighbors to report to the court for questioning.

Hangzhou

Relief for Farmers in Three Counties on the Zhejiang Border

The people of Longquan, Qingyuan, and Jingning counties in southern Zhejiang Province mostly rely on growing water shield (Gorgon fruit) for a living. In years of good harvest, the total income can be over one million yuan. However, the industry has been declining in recent years. The total winter shield business is less than 300,000. The water shield farmers are unable to continue planting and are seeking to return to their hometowns or even resorting to desperate measures. Chen Shizheng, the Administrative Inspector of the Second Special District, has ordered each county to establish a water shield production cooperative to provide relief, and also formed a general cooperative. They borrowed 90,000 yuan from the banking industry and distributed it to each cooperative. The Department of Finance and Construction submitted a proposal to the provincial government for approval, sending personnel to investigate the situation of the cooperatives and to negotiate loans with the banks in order to maintain the livelihoods of the farmers.

Letter to the Editor 92

To the Editor: I am writing regarding the article "Judge Investigates Corpse-Stealing Case" in the Songjiang News section of your paper on the 24th of this month. I find that the facts are not in accordance with the truth and hereby request a correction as follows. The ownership of the land in question belongs to the Jiazi War Memorial Association, which holds two certificates issued by the Ministry of Finance. Yin Wuben's household owns 7.86 mu, and Zhang Shude's household owns 6.148 mu. It has also been registered with the Songjiang County Government, and there is a record of grain transfer. During the war between Qi and Lu, Songjiang was a strategic location in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, and large numbers of troops gathered here. American missionary Bu Huilian maintained local order and provided relief to refugees, which was greatly appreciated by the people of Songjiang. They raised funds to build a pavilion here to commemorate this. This led to the founding of the Association. Later, because the pavilion was too high and was about to collapse, a meeting of directors and supervisors was held at the County Chamber of Commerce on the 22nd of September, 1933. A public discussion was held to rebuild the memorial pavilion and develop a park. The land was leveled and the half of the pavilion was demolished in February of this year. When skeletal remains were discovered, they were immediately reburied. All expenses, in addition to the 120 yuan provided by missionary Bu, were raised by members of the Association. The dismantling of the pavilion was in fact for the purpose of rebuilding it, as can be proven by Missionary Bu. The land is commonly known as Nijiatan, or Huchong, totaling 6.934 mu. The river mud is piled up like a mountain. It is neither a scenic spot in Songjiang nor a place where loyal souls are buried. The county gazetteer clearly states that the righteous soldiers who died during the late Ming Dynasty, including Dai Hong and 30 others, were buried behind the Dacheng Hall of the Confucius Temple in the city. The burial place of the Hong Yang rebel army is not recorded in the gazetteer. Since the Association built the memorial pavilion on this site in 1925, it has been protected by fences and wire mesh. No coffins have ever been buried here. Therefore, the story of the wounded soldiers being buried in 1927 is a fabrication, a distortion of the facts. I urge your newspaper to promptly issue a correction. Tang Zhi, representative of the Songjiang War Memorial Association. July 27th, 1935.

President Kong's Arrival in Shanghai Yesterday to Discuss Central and Local Disaster Relief Efforts 93

Sixth Plenary Session to be Convened According to Party Charter; Wang's Illness Improves, Xu Mo Temporarily Fulfills Foreign Ministry Duties

Central News Agency reports: Kong Xiangxi, Acting President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance, along with Xu Kan, Vice Minister of Finance, and Fu Rulin, Chairman of the Yangtze River Water Conservancy Commission, departed Nanjing by overnight train the night before last, arriving at the North Railway Station at 7:15 yesterday morning. They immediately returned to their private residence on Avenue Road to rest. Later, at around 11 a.m., they went to the Central Bank to handle important matters and met with Song Ziwen, Standing Committee Member of the National Economic Commission; Song Ziliang, General Manager of the National Products Bank; Zeng Rongfu, Director of the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund; Wen Qiao Xing, Commander of the Revenue Police Corps; Zhang Ming, Councilor of the Military Affairs Commission; Xu Hongbin, Councilor of the Executive Yuan's Peiping Political Readjustment Committee; and reporters from various newspapers. Jiang Bocheng Returns to Shanghai from Sichuan Yesterday; Will Visit Nanjing Again Before Returning to Guangdong 94

Notice from the Industry and Commerce Loan Association: Review of Credit Loan Applications Begins; Application Forms Delivered to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Yesterday for Distribution; National Products Factories Can Obtain and Fill Out Forms from the Chamber; Personnel from Various Banks and Firms Met Yesterday to Discuss Work Assignments 96

Xin Xin News Agency reports: The Municipal Industry and Commerce Small Credit Loan, managed by the Loan Committee, is scheduled to begin processing on August 1. It was also decided that application forms would be sent to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for distribution. It is learned that the various forms prepared by the Chamber, including the loan application form, application report, balance sheet, profit and loss statement, and a description of the small credit loan, have been printed and were sent to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce with a letter yesterday for distribution. An official notice was also published to announce the start of the review and lending process. As for the application procedures, they will generally follow the instructions in the description. Details are extracted below:

Notice Regarding Loan Processing

The Loan Committee issued a notice yesterday announcing the commencement of small credit loan lending, stating, "As per the order from the Ministry of Finance promulgating the Detailed Rules for Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loans, we are instructed to comply accordingly. The Detailed Rules stipulate that small credit loans for industry and commerce will be reviewed and lent by this Committee. It is hereby announced that processing will commence on August 1. All loan application forms, application reports, balance sheets, profit and loss statements, and instructions have been sent to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce for distribution to various trade associations, for applicants within those industries to fill out and submit to this Committee for review. Factories and firms that are not members of trade associations can directly obtain application forms from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and submit them to this Committee for review. Detailed procedures are all contained in the instructions. Applicants should pay special attention to this notice."

Talks Held Yesterday

The Industry and Commerce Loan Review Committee, in accordance with Article 10 of the organization charter approved by the Ministry of Finance (this Committee may borrow personnel from related banks and firms to handle investigation and review matters), sent letters to various banks and firms, requesting them to send personnel to participate. To date, over twenty personnel have been sent by various banks and firms. Cai Zengji, Chairman of the Committee, held a discussion meeting at 2 p.m. yesterday at the National Products Bank on the second floor to discuss investigation and review procedures and assign tasks. The meeting lasted for about an hour before adjourning. According to Xin Xin News Agency reporters, the personnel sent by various banks are all volunteers and receive no salary.

Forms Sent to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce

After deciding to commence lending on August 1, the Loan Committee had the drafted loan application forms, application reports, balance sheets, and profit and loss statements printed. A total of over 3,000 copies were sent to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce with a letter at 2 p.m. yesterday for distribution to various trade associations. The Chamber immediately sent a portion to various trade associations for applicants in those industries to fill out. Factories and firms that are not members of trade associations can directly obtain the forms from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce from today onwards, fill them out according to the various forms, and submit them to the Loan Committee for review.

Description of Credit Loan

Description of the Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Review Committee's Small Credit Loan: (1) Total amount: 5,000,000 yuan. (2) Requests for credit loans are limited to factories manufacturing national products, businesses selling national products, and those transporting national products for export. (3) In order to ensure that industry and commerce evenly enjoy the benefits of these credit loans, the maximum loan amount is limited to 5,000 yuan. (4) The credit loans are specifically for maintaining production and cannot be used to repay old debts. They cannot be used for speculative ventures or any other improper purposes. Otherwise, once discovered, this Committee will report to the government and prosecute according to the law on embezzlement of public funds. Goods and items purchased with the loans cannot be mortgaged elsewhere. Borrowers should submit monthly expense reports to the Committee for review. (5) Credit loan application forms and other forms will be sent by this Committee to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for distribution to various trade associations, for applicants in those industries to fill out and return to this Committee at the National Products Bank, 2nd floor, at the intersection of Henan Road and Tianjin Road for investigation and review. Factories and firms that are not members of trade associations may also obtain the above forms from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and submit them to this Committee for review. (6) Applicants should fill out the application form, together with guarantees from two reputable firms (if it is a limited liability company, the company manager must provide the guarantee), and a balance sheet and profit and loss statement (these documents must be certified by a CPA, bank, firm, or reputable business). Once approved, the loan will be issued. (7) If the applicant is also a guarantor for other credit loans, the approved loan amount will be calculated by combining the amount guaranteed. For example, if the applicant is qualified for a loan of 10,000 yuan but has a guarantee liability of 3,000 yuan, they can only borrow 7,000 yuan themselves. (8) The Committee incurs substantial expenses in handling loan investigations. Following established practices, applicants will be charged an investigation fee of 2 yuan to cover these costs. This fee should be paid to the Committee when submitting the application form, and a receipt will be issued. If the application is not approved, the fee will be refunded upon presentation of the receipt. (9) Applicants should carefully note all the provisions of the Loan Rules promulgated. (10) This Committee may reject applications that are incomplete or do not comply with the loan regulations. (11) The Committee's application form and other forms are as follows: (1) Application form, (2) Application report, (3) Balance sheet, (4) Profit and loss statement. If applicants are unable to fill out the forms correctly, they may seek assistance from someone experienced in modern bookkeeping (such as a CPA or a bank accountant).

Loan Application Form

Credit Loan Application Form, No. [Number] (IOU No. [Number]): Dear Sirs, I intend to borrow [Amount] yuan (national currency) from your Committee for a term of [Number] months, with the principal and interest to be repaid in full upon maturity. If approved, I will issue a separate IOU upon receiving the loan, with two firms providing separate or joint and several guarantees for repayment. I am submitting two copies of the Credit Loan Applicant Report, with all items filled out accurately, and attaching a balance sheet and a profit and loss statement, allowing your Committee to send personnel for investigation. I will accept your Committee's decision, whether approved or denied, without objection and will not inquire about the reasons for rejection. To the Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Review Committee, Applicant: [Name], [Date].

Applicant Report

Credit Loan Applicant Report: Account Name, Business Type, Address, Secondary Business, Affiliated Companies and Branches, Amount Requested, Repayment Period, Interest Rate, Purpose, Approved Amount by the Committee, Guarantor, A. (1) Total Capital, (2) Reserve Fund, (3) Names of Partners/Sole Proprietors/Shareholders, (4) Shareholders' Assets and Operations, (5) Manager's Name, (6) Manager's Brief History, (7) Years in Operation, (8) Current Total Business Volume, Total Funds Needed, (9) Relationship with Which Money Houses/Banks, (10) Outstanding Debts, (11) Profit and Loss Situation for the Past Three Years, (12) Last Year's Total Business Volume, Including (1) Wholesale, (2) Retail, (13) Source of Goods, (1) Purchased from Where, (2) Business Name, (3) Cash or Credit, (14) Sales Channels, (1) Sold To Where, (2) Business Name, (3) Cash or Credit, B. (1) Type of Company, (2) Total Capital Stock, (3) Reserve Fund, (4) Stock Par Value, (5) Stock Market Price, (6) Names of Unlimited Liability Shareholders, (7) Unlimited Liability Shareholders' Assets, (8) Names of Directors with Limited Liability, (10) Manager/Factory Director's Brief History, (11) Is it Registered?, (12) Years of Operation, (13) Current Total Business Volume, Total Funds Needed, (14) Relationship with Which Money Houses/Banks, (15) Profit and Loss Situation for the Past Three Years, (16) Last Year's Total Business Volume, (17) Last Year's Expenses Included (1) Salaries, (2) Rent, (3) Other, C.
