Japanese Commentator Takashige Murofushi's Assertions: Advocates for the Complete Withdrawal of Japanese Military Attaches from China; Japan Should Avoid Aggression, and Only Then Can China and Japan Approach Each Other 97

Yesterday's Japanese Mainichi Shimbun reported that Takashige Murofushi, a prominent contemporary Japanese commentator, departed from Tokyo on the 8th of this month to inspect various parts of North China. After visiting key figures in Nanjing, he arrived in Shanghai on the 23rd. On the 24th, Japanese reporters visited him at the Towa Hotel. He frankly expressed his views on Sino-Japanese relations, Japan's attitude towards China, and the mission of the Japanese people, as follows:

(1) Regarding the "Shinsei" Disrespect Incident: Articles disrespectful to Japan are not unique to China; they are frequently seen in other foreign countries as well. However, singling out China, whose military and national strength is weaker than Japan's, and making a big fuss over it is not the attitude of a great nation. If China is oppressed over every trivial matter, there will be no hope for adjusting Sino-Japanese relations.

(2) Regarding China's Anti-Japanese Movement: After Japan caused the Manchurian and Shanghai incidents, the demand that China prohibit the anti-Japanese movement should first examine the reasons for the previous anti-Japanese sentiment. Chinese people, in terms of national sentiment, have historically never had any reason to oppose Japan. After the anti-British movement broke out in the past, it gradually diminished due to the skillful policies of the British. Later, they gradually developed a dislike for Japanese imperialism, and a segment of the population wantonly engaged in anti-Japanese activities. However, if Japan had no reason to incite the emotions of the Chinese people, even if a portion instigated the entire nation, would they all follow suit?

(3) Regarding His Views on Chiang and Wang: The world considers Chiang and Wang not to be absolute power holders, which is a fundamental misconception. In reality, Chiang and Wang are great figures representing the civil and military aspects of China.

(4) Japan's Attitude Towards China: Japan, with the Imperial Way as its foundation, is at a time of great development. However, Japan must not adopt the aggressive policies of the 19th-century European and American powers. It should establish itself openly and uprightly, uphold justice, and soldiers must have the attitude of soldiers, properly fulfilling their shared responsibilities. Some have said that Manchuria is a "paradise" for independent states, but is this really the case? If Manchuria is an independent state, then suppressing bandits should be left entirely to the Manchurians. Japan should not sacrifice its own lives to maintain the security of other countries. Furthermore, in China, using means other than diplomatic channels to pressure the National Government and the Kuomintang is a fundamentally wrong policy. In my opinion (Murofushi stated), in order to adjust Sino-Japanese relations, all Japanese military attaches stationed in China should be withdrawn, leaving no one behind. At the same time, the strength of the Kwantung Army should be reduced by one-tenth.

(5) Criticism of Japanese Military's Infringement on Authority: Soldiers should handle direct issues fairly and openly, and should not fabricate or invent things. The Japanese military has repeatedly infringed on authority. For example, the disturbances in Manchuria and Shanghai are not called "wars" but "incidents," because incidents do not require the approval of the Diet or the deliberations of the Privy Council. In reality, so-called incidents are wars, carried out solely based on the intentions of the military, which is an infringement on authority. Therefore, in my humble opinion, focusing solely on small matters lacking transparency causes me great concern for the future of Japan.

Translator's note: Takashige Murofushi is a leading figure in the Japanese commentary world, with extensive writings and familiarity with the situation in China. He was commissioned by the Tokyo Yomiuri Shimbun to come to China to observe the actual situation. His sharp pen and precise insights are admired throughout Japan. It is said that he has written a systematic "China Travelogue" about his travels in China, which will be published daily in the Yomiuri Shimbun. Once the newspaper arrives, more will be translated.

National Silver Trade Deficit Exceeds 6 Million Yuan in the First Half of This Year 98

Shen Shi News Agency reports: The national gold and silver import and export situation for the first half of this year shows that silver outflow has decreased, with a trade deficit of nearly 6 million yuan. The gold trade surplus has also decreased compared to the same period last year. According to detailed statistics obtained by Shen Shi News Agency reporters, the national silver imports for the first half of the year totaled 2,925,000 yuan from Great Britain, 5,556,208 yuan from Hong Kong, 52,899 yuan from Japan, and 244,353 yuan from other countries, totaling 8,778,460 yuan (national currency). This is an increase of over 2 million compared to the import figure of 6,071,539 yuan for the same period last year. On the export side, 33,787 yuan were shipped to Annam, 1,967,050 yuan to Hong Kong, 707,080 yuan to Japan, and 54,320 yuan to the United States, totaling 2,862,237 yuan (national currency). This is a decrease of far more than 14 times compared to the export figure of 14,271,597 yuan for the same period last year. The silver trade deficit for the first half of the year was 5,916,223 yuan. Regarding gold imports and exports, the national imports for the first half of this year totaled 112,117 Customs Gold Units, an increase of over 100,000 Customs Gold Units compared to the import figure of 5,856 units for the same period last year. Gold exports totaled 13,969,110 Customs Gold Units, a decrease of over 4 million Customs Gold Units compared to the export figure of 18,175,344 units for the same period last year. The trade surplus for this year was 11,856,993 Customs Gold Units, a decrease of several million yuan compared to the surplus for the same period last year. In June alone, the gold trade surplus was 23,990 Customs Gold Units, and the silver trade surplus was 48,058 yuan (national currency). Therefore, the gold and silver trade situation this year is much better than last year.

National Grain Imports Exceed 100 Million Yuan in the First Half of This Year; Account for Over One-Fifth of Total Imports for the Half-Year; Sharp Increase in Rice Imports; Significant Value of Wheat Imports 100

Shen Shi News Agency reports: Our country is based on agriculture, but in recent years, the import of foreign grains has increased. Last year, due to drought in various provinces, our agricultural products were greatly reduced. This year, not only is foreign rice being imported in large quantities, but wheat imports are also considerable. Grain imports, including other miscellaneous grains, have reached over 100 million yuan in the first half of the year, accounting for one-fifth of the total imports for the half-year. Shen Shi News Agency reporters learned the following details from the Customs Office yesterday:

Rice Imports Exceed 70 Million

In the first half of the year, the national import of foreign rice totaled over 11 million metric tons, valued at over 75 million yuan (national currency). This included 8,093,627 Customs Gold Units from India, 25,074,763 Customs Gold Units from Annam, 100,511 Customs Gold Units from Hong Kong, 47,297 Customs Gold Units from Japan, 10,046,107 Customs Gold Units from Siam, 4,246 Customs Gold Units from Singapore, 31,047 Customs Gold Units from Dalian (Japanese rice), and 51,051 Customs Gold Units from other countries, totaling 43,359,190 Customs Gold Units, equivalent to 75,672,815 yuan (national currency). This is an increase of almost double compared to the import figure of 40,733,423 yuan for the same period last year and ranks first among foreign goods imported in the first half of the year.

Wheat Imports Also Show a Sharp Increase

In the first half of this year, not only were national rice imports huge, but wheat imports were also considerable. During the half-year, 1,054,156 metric tons were shipped from Argentina, valued at 3,752,863 Customs Gold Units; 3,299,795 metric tons from Australia, valued at 12,688,175 Customs Gold Units; 10,124 metric tons from Canada, valued at 47,748 Customs Gold Units; 48,281 metric tons from the United States, valued at 196,310 Customs Gold Units; and 28,099 metric tons from other countries, valued at 97,933 Customs Gold Units. In total, wheat imports amounted to 4,440,455 metric tons, valued at 16,783,029 Customs Gold Units, equivalent to 29,428,110 yuan (national currency). This is also an increase compared to the import figure of 15,194,783 Customs Gold Units for the same period last year.

Miscellaneous Grain Imports: The Total Value is Alarming

In addition to the large imports of foreign rice and wheat, this year's imports of other miscellaneous grains included 1,200,695 Customs Gold Units for bran, 171,408 Customs Gold Units for unnamed miscellaneous grains, 111,337 Customs Gold Units for sago, 1,863,097 Customs Gold Units for wheat flour, and 352,605 Customs Gold Units for unnamed miscellaneous grain flour. Including rice and wheat, the total value reached 63,841,361 Customs Gold Units, equivalent to 111,166,3759 yuan (national currency). This accounts for over one-fifth of the total value of foreign trade imports for the first half of this year, a truly alarming figure.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Convened Representatives from Various Factories to Guide Workers' Literacy Education; More Than Six Hundred Factory Representatives from Across the City Attended; Director Pan and Jiang Jianbai, Among Others, Attended to Provide Guidance 101

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce convened representatives from factories across the city at its assembly hall yesterday morning at nine o'clock to guide workers' literacy education. Chairman Yu Zuoting delivered the opening remarks, and Jiang Jianbai, a member of the Literacy Education Committee, reported on the implementation methods. Pan Gongzhan delivered a speech, and Wu Yun-Chu gave a lecture. The meeting adjourned at 11:30 am. Details are as follows:

Factory representatives attending included representatives from Tianchu Monosodium Glutamate Factory, Zhonghua Book Company, Central Mint, Rongmao Wood Factory, China Steel Buckle Factory, Double Wheel Toothbrush Factory, Kaicheng Acid Manufacturing Factory, Shanhai Marble Factory, Shenghelong Oil Factory, Weitong Yarn Factory, Wuhe Weaving Factory, Zhongfu Silk Factory, Huacheng Canvas Factory, Renfeng Dyeing and Weaving Factory, Dadong Bookstore, Jingyi Leather Factory, Zhongxin Textile Factory, Huatong Electrical Machinery Factory, Fufeng Flour Mill, Fuxin Flour Mill, Mianhua Commercial Electric and Gas Company, Zhufeng Enamel Company, Yifeng Enamel Factory, Samsung Cotton and Iron Factory, Commercial Press, Xiekang Tire Factory, China Chemical Industrial Society, Yihe Weaving Factory, Zhabei Water and Electricity Company, Nanyang Tobacco Company, Taikang Canned Food Factory, Zhonghua Enamel Factory, Zhongnan Cotton Weaving Factory, Meifeng Silk Weaving Factory, Guanshengyuan, Fuan Electric and Gas Factory, Da Zhongyang Rubber Factory, Pudong Electric Company, Dongfangnianhong Company, Baotai Silk Factory, Jiangnan Paper Factory, Guang Shenghang Factory, Hengfeng Silk Weaving Factory, Tonghe Cloth Factory, Longzhang Paper Factory, Home Industry Society, Linsheng Military Uniform Factory, Youlian Glass Factory, Yichangheng Carpet Factory, and more than 500 others. Representatives Wu Yun-Chu, Qiu Zhaolin, Wang Zhaozhang, Guan Bingqing, Shi Jiuyun, Huang Jingfan, and more than 600 others, along with Lu Jingshi of the Municipal Party Committee, Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Education Bureau, Wu Huanru, Section Chief of the Social Affairs Bureau, and Jiang Jianbai of the Literacy Education Committee, all attended to provide guidance.

Chairman's Opening Remarks

Yu Zuoting, Chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, recorder Zhu Guilin, master of ceremonies Tan Fengyan, and receptionists Wang Gang, Zhang Zhenyuan, Nie Haifan, Zheng Gongbi, and Xie Chenghsun, after performing the customary formalities, Yu Zuoting first delivered the opening remarks, saying, "Today, our Chamber of Commerce is convening everyone here because the municipal government has announced the implementation measures for workers' literacy education, ordering all factories to establish workers' literacy schools within a prescribed period. Our Chamber of Commerce has specifically convened representatives from various factories to comply with the government's orders and establish workers' literacy schools within the deadline. We have also invited Director Pan Gongzhan of the Education Bureau, Lu Jingshi of the Municipal Party Committee, Jiang Jianbai of the Literacy Education Committee, and Wu Huanru, Section Chief of the Social Affairs Bureau, to provide guidance," and so on.

Report on Implementation Measures

Following this, Jiang Jianbai reported on the methods for workers' literacy education, saying, "After Shanghai launched the literacy movement, and having established workers' literacy education measures, all illiterate workers within the city's boundaries must receive literacy education. Workers who are required to receive literacy education must, after receiving the enrollment notice from the literacy school or workers' school, if they delay or fail to enroll without reason, be subject to a fine of one dime to five yuan, or two hours to five days of labor service, in addition to being ordered to enroll within a prescribed period. The same applies to those who are absent from classes without reason. Workers who are required to receive literacy education, if they still have not received literacy education by July 1, 1936, will be ordered to stop working immediately until they have completed their literacy education, at which point they will be allowed to resume work. Factories, companies, shops, etc., that employ workers and staff who are required to receive literacy education, when they have 30 or more such individuals, should establish workers' literacy schools to conduct worker literacy education. When they have fewer than 30, their literacy education will be handled by the municipal literacy schools. The expenses of the schools will be borne by the respective factories, companies, shops, etc. If it is inconvenient to establish their own workers' literacy school, they may, depending on the number of illiterate workers, pay a fee of one yuan per person and request the Municipal Literacy Education Committee to handle it on their behalf. Factories, companies, shops, etc., that should establish workers' literacy schools, in any of the following circumstances, will be subject to a fine of up to 100 yuan, and will also be ordered to comply within a prescribed period: (A) failing to establish a workers' literacy school by August 31, 1935; (B) failing to ensure that all workers and staff who are required to receive literacy education have completed their literacy education by July 1, 1936. All factories, companies, shops, etc., within the city should conduct their own survey of the literacy and illiteracy status of their employed workers, including staff: (A) Those who have graduated from people's schools or other equivalent schools and hold relevant diplomas should submit the names of these workers and their graduation certificates to the district office of the Shanghai Municipal Literacy Education Committee. After verification by the district office, they will be recognized as literate workers and exempt from literacy education. (B) Those who can recognize the 600 characters stipulated by the Shanghai Municipal Literacy Education Committee should submit a list of these workers to the district office of the Shanghai Municipal Literacy Education Committee. After passing a periodic examination conducted by the district office, they will also be recognized as literate workers and exempt from literacy education. (C) Workers who do not fall into categories A or B will be considered illiterate workers and must receive literacy education. Workers' literacy schools should have a standard class size of 50 people, with men and women taught in separate classes as a matter of principle, according to the number of illiterate workers and the financial situation of the respective factories, companies, shops, etc. However, at least one class must be established before August 31, 1935, and the literacy education of all workers required to receive literacy education must be completed before June 30, 1936. Each class should have a standard teaching time of one hour per day. In special circumstances, with the approval of the district office of the Municipal Literacy Education Committee, this may be increased or decreased as appropriate. The best time for classes each day is before work in the morning, followed by after work at noon and before work in the afternoon. Except in cases of absolute necessity, classes should not be held after work in the afternoon. For those who work ten hours or less per day, class time may be outside of work hours. For those who work more than ten hours, class time should be within work hours. The duration of study should generally be two months. In special circumstances, with the approval of the district office of the Municipal Literacy Education Committee, the duration of study may be shortened or extended as appropriate. Budget standards, assuming the establishment of two workers' literacy school classes, the budget for start-up costs and monthly recurring expenses: (A) Start-up costs: eight yuan; (1) one large blackboard: five yuan; (2) one handbell: one yuan; (3) other (such as stationery for teachers): two yuan; (B) Recurring expenses: twenty-two yuan per month; (1) teacher's salary: fifteen yuan per month; (2) student stationery costs: five yuan per month; (3) miscellaneous expenses: one yuan per month; (4) school worker's allowance: one yuan per month. Preparatory steps: Factories, companies, shops, etc., establishing workers' literacy schools may follow the following steps: (1) determine the budget; (2) decide on the number of classes to establish; (3) appoint a teacher to be responsible for preparation; (4) select a school site and arrange the classroom; (5) determine the opening date; (6) submit a report on the opening; (7) open the school; (8) apply for registration. Within one week of opening, fill out the registration form and student roster in duplicate and request registration from the district office and the Chamber of Commerce." The speeches from Director Pan and Wu Yun-Chu are omitted here.

Tan Zhen Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday to Discuss Publication Law and the Judiciary; Emphasis on the First Instance After Implementing the Three-Tier, Three-Trial System 102

Tan Zhen, Vice President of the Judicial Yuan, arrived in Shanghai at the invitation of Central Committee Member Li Shizeng to prepare the Huang Keqiang Memorial Room for the martyrs. Tan arrived in port yesterday morning at 7:15 am by overnight train from Beijing and went to rest in a mansion in West Shanghai. A reporter from Riri News made a special visit to interview him, asking about the revised publication law. After it was passed by the Legislative Yuan, the national press felt that the implementation of the new law would be extremely difficult, and many telegrams were sent to the central government requesting reconsideration. Tan's opinion on this was very detailed, and he also discussed the problems of rectifying the national judiciary. The following is a detailed record:

Opinions on the Revised New Publication Law

Tan first spoke about the content of the revised publication law passed by the Legislative Yuan, saying, "I believe that the law itself does not have many flaws. However, the implementation of national laws seeks to be applicable. If the implementation of the law causes obstacles in society, it will violate the purpose of legislation and should be modified. Therefore, this issue needs to be studied. I think the three standards for banning publications passed by the Central Political Council this time are very appropriate."

Views on Private Matters

Regarding the section prohibiting the publication of personal and family private matters, the so-called private matters do not have a fixed scope, but should be interpreted as matters related to morality that do not need to be disclosed. Otherwise, there will be no restrictions. In the future, there will be a certain scope of regulations. Legislators intend to balance the legal interests of society and individuals. All countries in Europe and the United States have similar laws. However, due to different customs, the regulations are different. Some people in the press believe that the publication law is specially aimed at the suppression of the news industry, which is not necessarily the case.

Judicial Conference Will Not Be Postponed

The National Judicial Conference is scheduled to be held on September 16 and will open on schedule without delay. Most of the preparations have been completed. At that time, presidents of courts at all levels in each province, chief prosecutors, and representatives of judges and prosecutors should attend the meeting in Beijing. In addition, representatives of the National Lawyers Association can attend six people according to the regulations.

Rectify the Judiciary, Focus on the First Instance

After the implementation of the three-tier, three-trial system, local courts in various places feel the lack of judicial funds and talents. The judicial authorities are paying close attention to this because the first instance is extremely important. The facts and evidence of all lawsuits can be investigated by the trial court. In the past, the primary courts often did not seriously deal with cases because of the lack of talent and many cases, resulting in congestion in the second and third instances, which had a great impact. The implementation of the three-tier, three-trial system is intended to rectify the first instance.

Decision to Stop the Inspection in the North

I originally planned to go north to inspect the judiciary in North China after returning from Europe. However, due to busy official duties, it was postponed again and again and has not been completed. Now, Wang Yongbin, Minister of the Ministry of Judicial Administration, is scheduled to depart from Beijing on the 27th (today) to inspect the judiciaries in the provinces of Hebei, Tianjin, Shandong, Henan, Anhui, Suiyuan, Shanxi, and Shaanxi. I don’t need to go now.

Preparing Huang Keqiang Memorial Room

Tan finally said that I came here at the invitation of Mr. Li Shizeng of the Central Committee. Li is currently staying at the World Society on Foch Road. The house was formerly the residence of martyr Huang Keqiang, and Huang died there. Now, he wants to open a memorial room in this house to commemorate his immortality. Mr. Li specially invited me here to discuss everything, and there are no other tasks. I plan to return to Beijing the day after tomorrow.

Since taking office, Luo Tong, president of the Shanghai Local Court, has devoted himself to court affairs and carefully planned them. Recently, from July to August of this year, court has opened at 7:00 am every morning to hear various cases, but the parties involved often do not report on time, so it is announced that the parties must not delay any longer. Postmaster General Chaphekar; Improving Postal Delivery Methods; Hoping That Senders and Receivers Will Pay Attention 104

Shanghai Postal District Postmaster General Chaphekar sent a letter to this newspaper yesterday, saying, "To the editor: Our Postmaster General would like to say a few words to all Shanghai residents, that is, the employers of the post office. Would your newspaper please sacrifice its precious space to publish them so that readers may be slightly helped in sending and receiving mail. It should be remembered that the public's desire for the improvement of the local post office is the same as what our Postmaster General hopes for. The bureau is working hard to reform and will not slack off. If our customers can fully cooperate, the effect will be even more considerable. Looking at various countries around the world, the public in cities similar to Shanghai seems to be less concerned about their mail than the people in Shanghai. The people of Shanghai not only regard changing addresses as commonplace, but also believe that whether or not the post office has been notified of the new address, or whether there are errors or incompleteness in the name, address, and house number on the mail, the mail will definitely arrive. This is probably due to their trust in the post office. A few years ago, Shanghai was smaller, and this could be done. Now, even if there are several possibilities, all sectors must know that since the city has expanded, the scope has become very broad. To ensure timely and accurate delivery of mail, the following points are necessary: 1. The name and address of the recipient (such as street name and house number, etc.) should be written as clearly as possible. 2. If residing in a one-story or rented group of houses, the floor or group in which the recipient lives should also be indicated. 3. If in a lane, the lane number and house number should be indicated together. 4. If the name and address on the mail are written in a foreign language, it would be helpful to add the street name and house number in Chinese, as this will speed up delivery. All such mail must be translated into Chinese before delivery and then sent to the mail carrier, which is time-consuming and inevitably hinders delivery. 5. Each household should install a mailbox or door slot of appropriate size at the entrance, where the mail carrier can easily reach it. Those residing in a one-story or rented group of houses should also install a mailbox at a suitable location at the entrance or in the hallway. These mailboxes are necessary and not only ensure accurate delivery and reduce errors and losses but also protect the mail. The post office's promotion of this method is not to force the public to send mail in this way. It is hoped that it will benefit both the mail carriers and the public. In the future, due to the trend of the times, it is possible that all mail may be stopped delivery to those who have not installed these mailboxes or door slots. 6. Mail carriers are strictly prohibited from delivering mail to the back door. 7. If a registered letter is delivered, the person responsible for receiving it should immediately sign a receipt as quickly as possible, as there are others who are eagerly waiting for their mail. No matter how loyal servants are, please do not trust them too much, as they may forget sometimes. Therefore, all mail for a certain person, no matter how the address is written, must be entrusted to the responsible person for proper receipt. If this is done, even if the recipient is out, the mail will eventually be delivered to the recipient intact. It should be known that once the mail has been delivered according to the address written on it, the post office's responsibility ends. 8. Those who often change addresses should rent a private mailbox at the post office to have a fixed address so that their mail will not fall into the hands of bad people. The post office only accepts and registers applications for changing addresses. If any accidents occur, the seller must bear the responsibility themselves, and the post office will not be liable for any responsibility. 9. Please do not argue with the mail carrier. Most mail carriers are well-intentioned, but misunderstandings often occur due to differences in dialect. If there are any difficulties, please report the details to the Postmaster General, who will immediately pay attention. Sending mail according to the following methods can also be of great benefit: 1. The name and address written on the mail must be clear and correct. 2. The stationery used must be good, especially the envelope. Cheap envelopes cannot withstand long-distance transportation, resulting in a large number of letters that cannot be delivered even with the best efforts of the post office's delivery staff. All seals should be properly glued and tightly sealed to prevent private opening. It should be known that private opening of mail does not occur in the post office but mostly outside the post office. 3. Please avoid entrusting others to send mail as much as possible. The trusted friend may be forgetful and leave the letter in his pocket for a long time before sending it. Even the most loyal servants often make mistakes, especially when the mail does not require a receipt from the post office to prove that it has been sent. For the sake of prudence, it is better to purchase some stamps in advance for use at any time. When sending mail, stick the stamps yourself and put them in the postal mailbox collected by the mail carrier, or send them directly to the post offices located throughout the city, which is more appropriate. If the public can follow the above points, the post office will receive great help, and all facilities will be able to better satisfy customers. We have long admired your newspaper's enthusiasm for public welfare, so we have sent this letter. We hope you will agree to publish it. Thank you very much. Sincerely, The Editor of Shen Bao, Shanghai Postal District Postmaster General Chaphekar, July 26, 1935, Republic of China.

Xihu Long-Distance Bus Company; Shareholders' Meeting Tomorrow; Complete Highway Accepted and Taken Over 105

The Xihu Highway will be opened to traffic on August 10 as scheduled. It has now been fully transferred by the Engineering Office to the Xihu Long-Distance Bus Company. The company has also assembled 65 buses in preparation for the opening of traffic. The issues of travel time and fares will be decided at a special shareholders' meeting to be held tomorrow (28th). The details are as follows:

Handover Completed

After the completion of the Xihu Highway, it has been inspected and accepted by Shen Baixian, Director of the Construction Department of Jiangsu Province, Mei Chengzhang, Director of the Engineering Office, Wang Yaolai, General Manager of the Xihu Long-Distance Bus Company, Zhu Kaichou, Manager, and others. It was fully transferred to the company for takeover by the Engineering Office the day before yesterday and was received yesterday.

Opening on Time

After the company took over the entire line, it is now actively preparing for the opening of traffic and has assembled 65 buses. Each bus can accommodate 50 passengers. The body is painted lake green, the bottom is blue, and the middle has two white lines, which is very beautiful. It is decided to hold the opening ceremony on August 10 as scheduled at Luyang Bridge, the border between Shanghai and Jiangsu Province.

Route

The company has hired workers to build the stations along the line, which have now been completed. It is now planned to divide the entire route into three sections: (1) Shanghai to Changshu, (2) Changshu to Wuxi, (3) Changshu to Suzhou. There will be 12 round trips each day. The fare is 3 cents per kilometer. During the opening period, it will be calculated at 80% of the price. It is heard that the press will be invited to try out the service before the opening of traffic.

Shareholders' Meeting

As for the issues of travel time and fares for each section, it has now been decided to announce them after being approved by the shareholders' meeting the day after tomorrow. In addition to a separate notice, this is a special announcement. The Board of Directors." In addition, the company's office moved to No. 50 Yuanfuri, Shanshan Road, Zhabei, yesterday for office work.

Chang An Returned to Shanghai After Escaping Danger; Entered Jiangnan Shipyard for Repairs; Insurance Association Jointly Surveyed 106

The Chang An, a ship of the Liji Shipping Company in Shanghai, runs on the route from Shanghai to Xinghua, Quanzhou, Fujian. This time, when sailing from Shanghai to Quanzhou, it hit a reef by mistake when it was about to reach the sea off Fuzhou. The bottom of the ship collided, but it was fortunate enough to escape by itself. Fearing danger at the time, the shipowner telegraphed the company and ordered it to return to Shanghai immediately to check the extent of the damage and then decide on a repair plan. The company also reported this to the Maritime Administration and the China Ship Insurance Association for notification. The ship returned to Shanghai yesterday and sailed to the Gaochangmiao Jiangnan Shipyard to enter the dock to check the extent of the damage for repairs. The Insurance Association also sent ship surveyors to conduct a joint survey.

Committee for the Revival of Industry and Commerce; Approved the Training Program; Establishing Training Classes and Holding Lectures; Paying Attention to Accounting Management and Sales 107

Since its establishment, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce's Committee for the Revival of Industry and Commerce has begun to work in groups. The Investigation Group has been researching and studying the procedures for conducting investigation work by jointly inviting experts and leaders from various industries to meet and discuss with the director and deputy director of the group, Xi Yushu and Xu Xiaochu, and the director and deputy director of each group every day. The Training Group also held its first meeting at 4:00 pm the day before yesterday. It was convened by Luo Qinghua, Director of the Group. Xu Xiaochu, Xi Yushu, Pan Xulun, Luo Qinghua, Zheng Chengqing, and Ren Jinpin attended. The meeting was chaired by Luo Qinghua and Ren Jinpin served as the recorder. First, Ren Jinpin read aloud the original text of the training program proposed by Luo Qinghua and Pan Yangyao, and then submitted the original proposal for discussion. In addition to passing the principles, the following five items were also resolved: (1) In addition to establishing training classes, two lectures will be held each month, and another method of communication will be formulated. (2) To enable the industrial and commercial circles to deeply understand the importance of accounting, industrial and commercial management, and commodity sales, the director of the group will invite experts to put forward important outlines and compile small booklets for training and publicity. (3) It is recommended that Pan Xulun and Xi Yushu be responsible for planning the compilation of booklets on accounting issues. (4) It is recommended that Pan Yangyao contact the Industrial and Commercial Management Society to discuss the compilation of booklets on commodity sales issues. (5) It is recommended that Luo Qinghua and Pan Yangyao discuss the compilation of booklets on commodity sales issues. The training group's work plan that was passed is recorded below: (Work Plan) The preliminary cause of this committee is investigation, and the basic work is training. There are thousands of aspects to training problems. It should be suitable for the purpose of the industrial and commercial circles. Like treating a disease, investigation work is diagnosis, and training work is a prescription. At present, observing the difficult situations of various factories, although the reasons are different, the main points are that accounting is chaotic, management is lax, and sales are weak, which seem to be the biggest problems. The work of this group is based on this strategy. The outline is as follows: (1) Organize research classes. This group intends to invite experts to provide practical guidance and open the following three classes: (A) Accounting Research Class, (B) Industrial and Commercial Management Research Class, (C) Commodity Sales Research Class. The above three items seem to be essential subjects at present. Using the spare time of the industrial and commercial circles, this committee will notify industrial and commercial firms in various industries to send personnel in charge of accounting management and sales to come to the meeting for research. Each class will have two lessons per week, each lesson lasting about 2 hours. A small fee will be charged for the handouts. The research period is three months for each subject. The teachers will be given a small travel allowance. Each class will start with 30 students. If there are too many students, they will be divided into classes for research. (2) Specially appointed experts provide on-site guidance. Opening classes for training is very beneficial to industrial and commercial employees. However, the nature of each industry and each factory is different, and the environments are different. In many places, it is necessary to have technical experts to provide on-site guidance and improvement. After investigation and research, this committee should recruit experts to be available for various industries and factories to invite to provide guidance at any time, especially in the following talents. Special appointments should be made first so that they can be consulted at any time: (A) Mechanical aspects, (B) Architectural aspects, (C) Chemical industry aspects, (D) Accounting aspects, (E) Management and organization aspects. (3) Train the staff of this committee. The staff of each group of this committee has close relationships with various industrial and commercial industries. All work has the need for contact. Self-importance and self-reliance are likely to spoil things, and perfunctory treatment is also contrary to the purpose of the establishment of this committee. Therefore, this group should also formulate methods for training the work of this committee and hand them over to this group for training to achieve perfection. In addition, for the training plans of various factories, employee management methods, and plans to improve the intelligence of service personnel, they should be implemented in order of priority, step by step, etc.

Filial Daughter Cao E Temple Nears Completion; Wang Xiaolai and Others Inspect Construction 110

The Cao E Filial Daughter Temple, destroyed by fire in 1929, had stood for approximately two thousand years since its establishment in the first year of the Yuanjia era of the Later Han Dynasty. The enduring faith of people from far and wide demonstrates that her extraordinary filial piety is eternally immortal. Successive dynasties, Song, Yuan, Ming, and Qing, all praised her, benefiting the moral fabric of society. Prominent figures Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yiting, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Zhang Xuanchu, Jiang Weiguo, Ren Fengkui, Zhang Deyi, and others, recognizing this, initiated fundraising for reconstruction. Three years have passed, but due to the economic downturn, the donations have been meager, falling short of the substantial amount of fifty to sixty thousand yuan. It is said that loans were taken out to construct the temple, and the initiators will further solicit donations in the future. It is reported that the main hall's ridge beam will be installed on August 1st, and Wang Xiaolai, Zhang Deyi, Ren Fengkui, He Zhongxiao, Pei Yunqing, and others plan to inspect the construction.

Nine Acres: Brothel Raided, Twenty-Five Opium Addicts Arrested and Sent to General Bureau Along with Paraphernalia 111

The Old North Gate Police Station, acting on a tip, raided No. 8 Ren'an Lane in Nine Acres, where a large-scale opium den was operating, selling opium and providing beds for smoking. Police Chief Shen, considering the current strict opium prohibition, deemed the unrecorded opium den a blatant disregard for the law. He secretly dispatched Inspector Xu Wenrui, along with Sergeant Gao Kui and other officers, to the premises at 9 PM the night before. They arrested twenty-five opium addicts, including Lü Ziying, Yao Genfa, Zhou Lifang, Tang Lianchi, Wang Asan, Zhang Zhongren, and seized four opium pipes, five opium lamps, and a large amount of other opium paraphernalia. All were taken to the station for investigation. According to Chief Shen's interrogation, the defendants' testimonies were evasive, denying being the den owner. The case, involving the strict opium prohibition, has been referred to the General Bureau for legal action.

Iced Shaved Incident Resulted in Death - Suspect Imprisoned for Three and a Half Years 113

Xu Heshang, a local resident, aged 44, lived at No. 8, Lane 310, Tangshan Road. He was a peddler. On the morning of the 17th of this month, at around 8 AM, he went to the Tongzhou Road vegetable market to buy vegetables and returned home. Passing by the Fuxingguan Congee Shop at No. 643 East Xihua Road, he saw a shaved ice stall run by Lu Axiao, a native of Nanxiang. Because of the hot weather and dry mouth, he ordered a cup of shaved ice for six copper coins. After finishing it, he forgot to pay, leading to an argument with Lu Axiao, which escalated into a fight. As a result, Xu suffered chest injuries and fell to the ground. The congee shop owner, Yang Xizeng from Zhenjiang, and the shop assistant, Liu Changlin from Yangzhou, intervened to stop the fight. Xu returned home and felt a slight pain in his chest. Two friends, Zhang Awei, went to the ice stall to negotiate with Lu, paying ten foreign triangular copper coins. Liu Changlin bought medicine on their behalf and gave it to Xu, who felt a little better. The next morning, Xu went to the South City to sell watermelons but suddenly felt pain under his chest again. He returned home and went to bed. At 1 PM in the afternoon, he suddenly died. Someone reported it to the Jiaxing Road Police Station, which sent detective Jin Yangwu to investigate. The body was taken to the forensic examination office on Pelleng Road, where prosecutor Guo Wei from the First Special District Court conducted an examination. Because Xu's injuries were internal, a forensic autopsy revealed that two ribs on the lower left chest were broken. He had a pre-existing lung condition. Lu Axiao was sent to the court for interrogation and detention. Yesterday morning, Judge Jiang Shuzi from the Third Criminal Court conducted a hearing. The Public Works Department's lawyer, Wang Yaotang, stated that according to the forensic examination, although the deceased had a lung condition, the cause of death was the broken ribs. After deliberation, according to the testimonies of Yang Xizeng, Liu Changlin, Zhang Awei, and Xu's wife, Zhang, about the incident, and the report, the judge determined that because the deceased did not pay for the shaved ice and cursed at the shop owner, who tried to slap him but failed. He then hit the shop owner, who resisted and pushed him, causing him to fall to the ground and hit an electric pole, breaking his ribs. Judge Jiang sentenced Lu Axiao to three years and six months of imprisonment, with two days of pre-trial detention counting as one day of imprisonment.

Money Exchange Shop Sues for Recovery of Share Capital; Hearing Concluded, Sentence to Be Announced Next Wednesday 114

The Rongkang Money Exchange in Tongji Lane, Tianjin Road, has been operating for many years. The shop's capital totaled 300,000 yuan, divided into ten shares, each worth 30,000 yuan, subscribed to by Sun Zhizhai, Wang Xiancheng, Xi Qisheng, and others as shareholders. In the winter of last year, some shareholders, including Gu Liancheng, had no intention of continuing the business. They planned to reorganize Rongkang Money Exchange into Rongkang Fengji Money Exchange and recruit new shares. The old Rongkang shareholders would subscribe to six shares, totaling 180,000 yuan, and four new shares would be recruited to facilitate the name change and business.

Among the new shareholders, a Russian doctor, Ding Jiwan, subscribed to one share. Another one-quarter share under Ding's name, worth 7,500 yuan, was attached by Dr. Zhu Xiangshan (aka Zhu Ziyun). Therefore, Ding issued a formal receipt. Although all the share capital for Rongkang Fengji Money Exchange had been collected, Rongkang Money Exchange, affected by the economic downturn, suddenly announced its closure on January 30th of this year, engaging a lawyer for formal liquidation. This affected Fengji Exchange,

preventing its official opening. The collected share capital could not be repaid immediately. Recently, Zhu Ziyun, whose share was attached to Ding Jiwan, engaged lawyer Lu Qijin and filed a complaint with the Criminal Court of the First Special District Court, accusing Rongkang Exchange's manager, Xi Qisheng, assistant manager, Qin Guangzhao, and associate, Zhu Pinsheng, of jointly breaching trust and embezzling the 7,500 yuan share capital. Ding Jiwan was also listed as a person of interest. The Special Court

had summoned them once, but because the defendants did not appear, the hearing was rescheduled. All details were recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Yang Zhaoting continued the hearing in the Eighth Criminal Court. The three defendants also arrived with their defense lawyer, Yuan Hanyun. Complainant Zhu Ziyun stated that in the winter of last year, he met Xi and Qin at Ding Jiwan's place. They solicited him to become a shareholder in Rongkang Fengji Money Exchange. Seeing that Ding had already joined, he agreed. The 7,500 yuan share capital was attached to Ding's name. At that time, Ding

issued a receipt, which was written by Xi and signed by Ding. He then gave Rongkang promissory notes to Xi and Qin. All share capital was claimed to have been fully collected and deposited in the Fuyuan and Anyu money shops. Unexpectedly, Xi and others later transferred the share capital to Rongkang Money Exchange, leading to its collapse. Rongkang Fengji Money Exchange also did not open. The defendants' actions constituted embezzlement and should be prosecuted. Xi Qisheng and others stated that they were the

Rongkang manager. Because Rongkang shareholder She Biancheng had no intention of continuing the business, they initiated a reorganization, adding Fengji to the name. The old Rongkang shareholders subscribed to 180,000 yuan, and Yu Zhendong, Lu Shaotang, Ding Jiwan, and others joined as new shareholders. Ding subscribed to one share, totaling 30,000 yuan. Complainant Zhu Ziyun was Ding's attached share, an undisclosed partner. The total capital of 300,000 yuan had been fully collected and initially deposited in the Fuyuan and Anyu money shops. But because Fengji Exchange was a reorganization of Rongkang,

all share capital should be transferred to Rongkang. This could be verified with the Money Exchange Association, as it was a common practice. Rongkang announced its liquidation on January 30th of this year. All the old Rongkang shareholders of Fengji expressed their willingness to repay the share capital, but it was only a matter of time. This case was entirely within the scope of civil matters. According to regulations, the complainant should negotiate with Ding Jiwan, who should then file a civil lawsuit against the defendants, which would be the proper course of action. It was inappropriate to rashly file a criminal lawsuit. After the lawyers for both sides argued, the court announced that the case would be adjourned and a sentence would be announced next Wednesday afternoon.

Rickshaw Merchants Submit Opinions in Letter; Taxpayer Association Forwards to Public Works Department for Correction on Two Points 115

Lu Dexing, Gu Songmao, Zhang Jingbo, Wang Runling, and five hundred other representatives of Shanghai's public rickshaw merchants, wrote to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association, stating: "We respectfully submit that since the Public Works Department's Vehicle Committee ordered the public rickshaws to adopt the new style, we rickshaw merchants have experienced hardship for years. The results have shown only disadvantages, with no benefits. As taxpayers, we respectfully bring this to your esteemed association's attention to protect taxpayers' interests and request your association to urge the Public Works Department to promptly make corrections to alleviate the merchants' difficulties. We present the two most important points below: (1) Vehicle style: The existing vehicle style adopted by us rickshaw merchants has been in use for twenty years. Both the riders and pullers find it satisfactory. The evolution of this style involved iron-clad wheels, then solid rubber wheels. With the advancement of transportation and the widespread installation of tram tracks on the roads, to avoid the wheels getting caught in the tracks and causing accidents, they were universally changed to inflatable rubber tires, which have been in use ever since without incident. The road traffic conditions today are the same as before, yet the Public Works Department suddenly issued an order for a so-called new style rickshaw, seemingly enforcing it mandatorily. To promote the new style, the Public Works Department is willing to increase the taxpayers' burden by 40,000 yuan annually, establishing a Vehicle Committee to oversee it. The committee was originally intended to last for eight months, but now it seems to be established permanently and unconditionally, further increasing the taxpayers' burden. The so-called new style is neither more convenient for the pullers nor provides any special comfort for the riders. It is merely expensive and difficult to place, harming the rickshaw merchants. To comply with the wishes of the Public Works Department's Vehicle Committee, the rickshaw merchants specially submitted a sample for inspection, requesting that, while maintaining the existing vehicle style, we be allowed to make improvements within our means. However, despite submitting this request many days ago, we have yet to receive any approval. Within the Vehicle Committee, only one person is diligently designing behind closed doors. This will only waste large sums of money without any practical benefit. In short, anything that requires mandatory enforcement must have minimal benefit and significant drawbacks. Otherwise, the Vehicle Committee's new style would naturally gain popularity without needing to be promoted or forced. The inconvenience of pulling the Vehicle Committee's new style is an undeniable fact. We rickshaw merchants are the ones who perform this labor, and our understanding of the advantages and disadvantages is not something that those who merely argue can comprehend. Therefore, the new style that rickshaw merchants are being forced to use must be abolished. We rickshaw merchants should strive to make improvements to the existing vehicles so that both pullers and riders are satisfied. (2) Rickshaw Mutual Aid Association: The rickshaw pullers' status is precarious due to their small business, weak individual strength, and lack of leadership. There has never been a comprehensive relief system. Recognizing this, the Public Works Department formulated a draft plan for managing and assisting rickshaw pullers last year, appointing responsible personnel to organize the association. All mutual aid funds are collected from the rickshaw pullers, with seven cents per day. This collection process is handled daily by the rickshaw merchants, who also have to prepay the fees when renewing licenses. This matter concerns the rickshaw pullers themselves, and we rickshaw merchants have no say in it. However, we rickshaw merchants not only bear the burden of collecting the fees but also the obligation to prepay them. Therefore, we feel compelled to speak out. The Mutual Aid Association aims to provide relief to rickshaw pullers, and the significance of this relief is substantial. Since the collection of mutual aid fees began, it has amounted to a substantial 180,000 yuan. However, the results of the relief efforts have been negligible, with the rickshaw pullers receiving virtually nothing. During the summer, the Public Works Department provides water buckets for horses pulling carts to relieve their thirst and prevent heatstroke, without collecting mutual aid fees from the horses. However, the rickshaw pullers are only subject to the sacrifice of paying mutual aid fees without receiving the right to relief. Now, in the heat of summer, they are proposing to set up only twenty-two teapots, which is insufficient. This is a great disparity in treatment between humans and animals. We also understand that the person in charge of the association's affairs is Dr. Zhu Maocheng, a former labor director who attended international labor conferences. We rickshaw merchants are greatly pleased to hear this and congratulate the rickshaw pullers, believing that Dr. Zhu will use his knowledge and experience to relieve the laborers and provide them with genuine assistance, making him a savior to the labor community. However, the actual results have been the opposite. There is still time to improve the situation. Given the urgent need during this hot weather, the rickshaw pullers should be provided with water bottles like those used by Boy Scouts or the military, numbered to match the vehicle licenses, and distributed to each vehicle to provide water for thirst. At the same time, each rickshaw puller should be given two bottles of "Seven Good" medicine and items like straw hats and running shoes to prevent heatstroke when walking under the scorching sun. If the substantial funds collected from the rickshaw pullers are not used to provide them with relief, how can Dr. Zhu answer to the rickshaw pullers who pay the mutual aid fees, to the Chinese directors who recommended him, and to the taxpayers who support his salary? The above two points are the common grievances and suffering felt by both rickshaw merchants and rickshaw pullers. We respectfully submit this and request your association to provide fair and impartial guidance and assistance. We humbly submit this and hope for your consideration, for the sake of virtue and convenience. We respectfully submit this to the Shanghai Public Concession Chinese Ratepayers' Association. The Taxpayers' Association has forwarded it to the Public Works Department."

The French Concession Municipal Council has been conducting rickshaw puller registration for two months, and the registration process has been enthusiastic. However, there are still a few rickshaw pullers who, influenced by others, are taking a wait-and-see approach. To expedite the completion of the registration, the council has decided on strict measures and announced that all rickshaw pullers must register promptly. The announcement states: "The French Concession authorities have recently discovered that certain organizations are obstructing the registration of rickshaw pullers. The authorities have decided on the following measures: (1) Starting August 1st, rickshaw pullers who do not comply with the registration regulations and hold licenses above number 16,000 will not be allowed to operate in the French Concession. (2) Starting August 1st, rickshaws whose pullers do not comply with the registration regulations and hold licenses above number 16,000 will be immediately detained. (3) Detained rickshaws will only be returned to the owners after the rickshaw pullers comply with the registration regulations. Regarding the registration dates for rickshaw pullers, in accordance with the French Concession authorities' regulations for rickshaw puller registration, this police station will begin processing the registration of rickshaw pullers with the following license numbers starting on August 1st of this year: August 1st to 10th: register numbers 15,501 to 16,000; August 12th to 20th: register numbers 15,001 to 15,500; August 21st to 31st: register numbers 14,501 to 15,000. Rickshaw pullers must bring their registration application forms (vehicles do not need to be brought) to No. 28 Xuehuali Road."

Two Dockyards Suggest Merger 117

In recent years, various industries have been in decline, and the shipping industry has inevitably been affected. There are few purchases of new ships, and shipping companies, in order to save expenses, are adopting a policy of minimizing ship repairs. There are two British-owned shipbuilding and ship repair companies in Shanghai: one is Ruirong, and the other is the Yiesonglao Dockyard. Recently, both have seen a significant decrease in work and are struggling to profit. Therefore, during the recent annual shareholders' meeting of the Yiesonglao Dockyard, a proposal was made for the two companies to merge their operations to avoid competing with each other and suffering losses together. The proposal will be reviewed by the board of directors and assisted by three or four major shareholders. After the review is completed and a written opinion is prepared, a shareholders' meeting will be convened for a decision.

Public Works Department Specifies Time Limits for Lung Disease Treatment in Various Hospitals 118

The Public Works Department's Health Committee, citing the increasing number of foreign lung disease patients and the inadequacy of existing lung disease beds in the Public Works Department's Isolation Hospital, as well as the lack of facilities for expansion, considered imposing time limits on long-term lung disease patients. It is reported that the Health Committee's regulations were approved by the board of directors at a recent meeting and have been implemented.

Hangzhou Buddhist Association Sues Cihang Weekly for Defamation; Details of Defamatory Facts and Violations Presented; Defendant Did Not Appear at Yesterday's Court Hearing 120

Master Quefei, 63 years old, from Fujian, the abbot of Lingyin Temple and a standing committee member of the Hangzhou Buddhist Association, Master Mutao, 40 years old, from Wuxing, the abbot of Fajing Temple, and Master Benlian, 39 years old, from Haining, recently filed a lawsuit because the Cihang Weekly (located at No. 254, Xiafei Road (intersection of Songshan Road)), published on June 17th of this year, an article about the re-election of the abbot of Liansi Temple in Hangzhou, which contained malicious defamation, accusing the Hangzhou Buddhist Association of not being a legitimate organization of monks. Although the abbots are

detached from worldly concerns, they must strictly adhere to the monastic rules. The defamed party is a group, and Hangzhou is a place where ancient Buddhist temples and cultural treasures converge. The association is the only religious organization legally registered. Therefore, the credibility is greatly affected. In their capacity as legal representatives of the association, they engaged lawyer Gu Kenfu to file a complaint with the Criminal Court of the Second Special Court, suing the Cihang Weekly for disseminating words to damage the reputation of the organization. The complaint stated that the weekly disseminated words defaming

a religious organization, failed to legally record the names of the publisher and editor, and filed a private lawsuit, along with civil charges. The complaint stated that the association is composed of monasteries in Hangzhou and has been registered with party and government agencies as a legitimate religious organization and has been repeatedly rewarded by the government for its social service. On June 17th of this year, the defendant published an article about the re-election of the abbot of Liansi Temple in Hangzhou, stating that the city's Buddhist association was not organized by legitimate monks and had repeatedly violated the law. These accusations were groundless and malicious. Although the monks are detached from worldly concerns, they must

adhere to the monastic rules. The defamed party is not a single individual but a group. Hangzhou is a major center of Buddhism, with many ancient monasteries. The association is the only representative organization of Buddhism in Hangzhou. Its credibility is greatly affected. This matter concerns the public, and silence cannot be maintained. The reasons for filing the private lawsuit are stated separately as follows: Regarding the defamation,

freedom of speech is essential. However, there must be true facts, and the facts must be related to public interest and subject to fair comment. This is the inevitable interpretation of the law. Reading the defendant's article, it is unfounded and maliciously accuses the association of being an illegal organization of monks and falsely states that the association has been involved in illegal activities. It is not known who the so-called illegal monks are or what illegal activities they have been involved in.

The defendant's actions violated Article 246, Paragraph 1, and Article 310, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Code and Article 261, Paragraph 1, and Article 325, Paragraph 2 of the old Criminal Code. Regarding the failure to record the names of the editor and publisher, the names of the publisher and editor of newspapers and magazines must be recorded, as stipulated in Article 12 of the Publication Law. According to Article 30 of the same law, publications without the records specified in Article 12 or with inaccurate records are subject to a fine of up to 200 yuan. Since its publication, the defendant has repeatedly made insinuations against monks. This time, it has defamed a public organization.

A thorough search of the newspaper revealed that there were no records of the names of the editor and publisher. The intention to evade responsibility after committing a crime is self-evident. The defendant's illegal actions violated Article 12 of the Publication Law and should be punished in accordance with Article 30 of the same law. Regarding the supplementary civil charges, the defendant's criminal actions directly damaged the association's credibility. The defendant should be responsible for restoring the association's reputation and compensating for the damage. To restore the reputation, the court must order that

the full text of the court's judgment be published in major newspapers in Shanghai and Hangzhou for three days, with the defendant bearing the cost. Regarding damages, the value of the association's reputation cannot be estimated with money. Therefore, we only request the court to order compensation of one yuan as a legal expression. Based on the above reasons, we request the court to promptly summon the responsible editor and publisher of the newspaper to court and punish them for their crimes, and in the supplementary

civil lawsuit, order the defendant to fulfill the plaintiff's request to maintain the law and protect the reputation of public organizations. Based on the complaint, the court opened the Second Criminal Court at 11:00 AM yesterday, presided over by Judge Qiu Huanying. The lawyer representing the plaintiffs stated the purpose of the complaint as above. No one from the defendant, Cihang Weekly, appeared in court. The court then ordered the plaintiff to investigate and report the names of the defendant's publisher, editor, and other personnel to the court for a rescheduled hearing and then adjourned.

Public Concession: Police Report for June 121

According to the Public Works Department's Fire Department's report for June, the department received a total of 70 fire alarms during the month, of which 4 were false alarms. According to statistics, the value of the property endangered by fire in the Public Concession this month was over 20 million yuan, while that in the Special Areas was over 40,000 yuan. However, the actual losses amounted to 73,093 yuan within the concession and 2,635 yuan in the Special Areas. The most significant fire in June was the burning of the Dahua Celluloid Toy Factory at No. 100, Lane 1371, Xiaoshadu Road, which claimed the lives of 23 people and injured 46 others. However, after the fire engines arrived at the scene, they quickly extinguished the fire, and the fire was brought under control in about half an hour.

Disaster Reports from Various Regions 122

Hunan Association in Shanghai: The office of the Hunan Drought Relief Association's representative in Shanghai received a telegram from Chairman He Hao of the Hunan Provincial Flood Relief Headquarters and a detailed letter from Cao Bowen, Director of the Hunan Civil Affairs Department, reporting on the forty counties affected by the disaster and the collapse of over a thousand embankments. The letter detailed the situation in the most severely affected counties of Hunan as follows: (1) Yiyang: On the 8th of this month, the Zi River experienced a flash flood, with the water level rising to several Zhang (丈 - approximately 3.3 meters). Areas such as He Xing, Hucheng, Gaojia, Yanhe, Wenjia, Datian, Paitou, Xujia, Tongyou, Jinhua, Xiaozhou, Shahe, Yongxing, Yonghe, and Changchun were flooded. Baolian, Nanmen, and Dugong were submerged, and fields, crops, and houses were completely destroyed. (2) Changde: Floodwaters from Chenzhou's Baihe River reached several Zhang, flowing downstream and reaching depths of over a Zhang in Changde's Nanmen area. The Baguan Embankment outside Dongguan collapsed. (3) Yueyang: From June 20th to July 3rd, the lake water rose by more than two Zhang. Small embankments throughout Hunan were submerged, resulting in the submersion of over 113,000 Mu (畝 - approx. 667 sq meters). (4) Anxiang: The Yuan and Feng Rivers flooded, submerging over 300,000 Mu of fields in Anxiang County, and drowning over 1,000 people. (5) Yuanjiang: 197 embankments of various sizes were breached, affecting over 200,000 people, with over 1,000 killed by the floods. (6) Cili: Starting in June, continuous heavy rain fell for five days and nights. The Lou and Feng Rivers rose more than six Zhang, turning the county seat and districts one, two, three, four, and five into a watery expanse, drowning over 10,000 people. (7) Lixian: At You Shi (5-7 PM) on June 5th, the city wall was breached by the floodwaters. The orphanage, poor people's factory, relief center, prison, girls' school, low-lying houses, shops, and people were all lost, buried in the bellies of fish. The estimated death toll exceeded 2,000 people. (8) Shimen: Since June 20th, continuous rain fell. On July 3rd and 4th, torrential rain fell in Cili for two full nights. From Nishan, Suoshi, Zaoshi, Yanshi, Zaoshi, Baishadu, Xinguang, Yijiadu, and Tongziping, hundreds of Li (里 - approx. 500 meters) were turned into a vast expanse of water. All buildings in the county, except for the county government which was spared from collapse, including other agencies, schools, shops, and civilian homes were reduced to rubble. The death toll exceeded 10,000 people. (9) In Hanshou County, over 300 embankments of various sizes were breached, and the loss of fields, homes, livestock, and human lives was incalculable.

Hubei Association: Yesterday, we received a telegram from Sun Zhounian, representative of the former inspection and relief deputy director, saying: "Guan Jiongzhi, Liu Wanqing, Gao Jianqing, and all village elders, please be advised. Our Hubei province is unfortunately facing overlapping calamities. The Red Scourge has not been quelled, and natural disasters continue to strike. The early drought caused immense suffering to the people. Before we could catch our breath, continuous heavy rains this summer led to flash floods, creating an unstoppable force. Xiang and Yun were the first to bear the brunt, followed by the Han River region. Embankments collapsed, unleashing devastation for thousands of Li. Jing and Sha became vast pools, and Hanyang was submerged. The Yangtze River surged, causing widespread flooding. The entire city of Hankou was nearly turned into a swamp. Fortunately, the military and civilians joined forces and worked through the night to avert a major catastrophe. Now that the river level has receded slightly, strong winds and waves persist. As we enter the flood season, water levels continue to fluctuate. Hankou, located at the confluence of the Yangtze and Han rivers, is a low-lying area facing constant danger. Despite the protection of the Zhang Embankment, years of disrepair have weakened its structure, making breaches imminent. The area affected by the floods has reached forty-nine counties, with hundreds of thousands of people dead and countless properties lost. Fields were washed away, houses were destroyed, and entire families of more than ten people tied themselves together and perished in the flood. Floating corpses drift everywhere, leaving the dead without burial. The situation is unspeakably tragic, with countless livestock lost. It is reported that Yangluo Town, located at the confluence of the Yangtze and Han rivers, is retrieving over a thousand corpses daily. The stench of decaying bodies is unbearable. This is a catastrophe unseen in a century. Natural disasters have struck, and the calamities have not ended. The dead are gone, but the living are in dire need. Millions of refugees are in urgent need of assistance. Some are clinging to rooftops and tile ridges, while others are taking refuge in corners of cities and treetops, exposed to the sun, dew, heat, and water. Cries of hunger and weeping fill the air, as lives hang by a thread. The suffering is so severe that even Zheng Xia's 'Refugee Picture' cannot fully capture its horror. Without swift aid, millions of survivors will die not only from the floods but also from starvation and disease. The situation is more severe than the great flood of 1931. People are on the verge of death, like lamps flickering in the wind, desperately seeking food like a great drought yearning for rain. We implore you, gentlemen, to show compassion and concern for your homeland, and to treat this unprecedented disaster as a call for action. Let us pool our resources, no matter how small, and gather strength to create a significant impact. Your efforts will not be in vain, and the people will benefit greatly. We rely on your generosity and compassion to bring relief and restore harmony. Your kindness will be remembered forever. The Yangtze River flows ahead, and we await your benevolent response. With tears in our eyes, we present this urgent appeal, hoping for your compassionate assistance. Sun Songnian and San Jiguang, on behalf of millions of flood victims, bow and plead."

We now present the recent relief reports as follows: (Hubei) The Chamber of Commerce of Laohekou City sent a telegram stating: "Since the 3rd of this month, heavy rain has fallen continuously for several days and nights. On the 5th, a flash flood occurred, submerging nearly all of the town's seventy streets and lanes. The water depth ranged from several Zhang to several Chi (尺 - approx. 0.33 meters). Countless people and livestock were swept away, and many houses collapsed. The rain stopped on the 8th, and the water receded slightly. The cries of mourning are unbearable. Countless people are without food or shelter. Transportation to surrounding areas has not yet been restored. We hear that hundreds of Li upstream and downstream have been affected, but the extent of the disaster is unknown. Our Chamber of Commerce has joined with various agencies and organizations to form a relief committee and is providing aid to accessible areas. However, the town's food supply is only sufficient for a few days. Raising funds is difficult, and finding food to purchase is impossible. The future is bleak. We are doing our best to make arrangements and will provide a detailed report with photos later. We urgently appeal for relief." (Henan) The educators of Yanshi County sent a telegram stating: "Since the Yi and Luo River flood of 1931, our county has suffered from severe drought, causing the people to become destitute and displaced. They have not yet recovered. Suddenly, on the 6th of this month, heavy rain fell. That night, the Yi and Luo Rivers flooded, roaring and surging. In an instant, the embankments were in danger. On the afternoon of the 8th, the embankments breached, flooding the city. The water level was as high as the city walls. By nightfall, the floodwaters were even more violent. The city and surrounding areas were submerged in a vast expanse of water. Mothers disregarded their own safety to save their children, and filial sons struggled to rescue their fathers. The cries of terror were heartbreaking. Corpses littered the streets, and a foul stench filled the city. Most of the houses were swept away. Those who managed to escape were left to sleep in the wilderness, without warm clothing or food. The scene was truly heart-wrenching. Along the riverbanks, for dozens of Li, the water merged with the sky. Over a thousand villages were turned into swamps. About five hundred people died, and almost no houses remained intact. Tens of thousands of acres of fertile land were covered in sand. The tragedy is beyond words. We urgently appeal for immediate assistance." (Anhui) Yang Jiaoguang and others, representatives of Zhang Gaobao in the third district of Dongliu, sent a telegram stating: "Zhang Gaobao, Dongliu County, is located near the river and is a low-lying area. Since June 21st, continuous heavy rains have caused flash floods and tidal waves to reverse flow, creating a confluence from both sides. The entire area has turned into a swamp. Houses and graves are submerged in water. Low-lying areas are submerged by 11 or 12 Chi, and short houses have completely disappeared. High-lying areas are submerged by 7 or 8 Chi. Those who have survived the disaster are once again suffering from this severe and unprecedented catastrophe. Like water becoming deeper and fire becoming hotter, we, the representatives, are heartbroken by the sight of the disaster. We urgently appeal for relief to save the victims." The Bright Star Discovered During the Day Is Actually Venus 124

In recent days, a bright star has been seen in the sky, visible even during the day. Groups of people on the streets of Shanghai have been looking up at it, speculating about its identity. Some say it is a lucky star, others say it is Jupiter. Now, according to Father Qi of the Xujiahui Observatory, it is actually Venus. The star is currently close to Earth, making it visible during the day, which is not uncommon.

China Library Fine Publication – Yuan Zhonglang Complete Works Published 136

The rebellious spirit is full of his poems, letters, travel notes, and essays. The Qing Dynasty was listed as a banned book and destroyed for more than 300 years.
